O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, my very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last part of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment and have made the end through its explanations and by its declarations. 
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would accomplish it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery". 
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is treated in our region and is foreign throughout, so the science is lost and decayed, and nothing remains of the virtues except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved. 
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and knowledge is driven away. 
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive it together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the shapes of the cautery irons, and the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary. 
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged. 
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for whoever undertakes this to be learned in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the placement of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of arteries, and the movement and rest of the veins, and their place of origin. 
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that skill without practice is much, and with work it is little; and the same in the art of surgery. 
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, beware lest he falls into error and harms people; so I have wanted many times more than those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves to their lack of knowledge and experience. 
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut open an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries in her neck; which caused so much blood to come out that the woman died in his hands. 
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And see another example which treats a stone of a man of age, and the stone was large; if he took with it a piece of the bladder, and died the man inside three days. 
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew that if it were cut out he would die. 
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see another surgeon who took in hand the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break he had a wound; and the surgeon full of ignorance pulled out the break on the wound as if it were a splinter with great force, and did not leave the wound any bandage, and left it like that at the end; and he ordered him not to untie it; and it remained so until his leg was all swollen and his foot and came to ruin. 
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come loosen the leg; and when I loosened it, he was so happy and did not feel any pain. 
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the way the corruption was already confirmed or in a limb, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to go through the limb until the limb was completely lost. 
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another wonder which drains the festering abscess, and then inflames through the malice of its ruler. 
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a sore, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not fitting that one touch it with iron unless it is in a place where one can remove all that is corrupted. 
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, work where there is danger in many positions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger. 
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason it is necessary that you guard yourselves, so that foolish people cannot speak ill of you. If you take up your arms in defense, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave the incurable diseases to their grief; and remove your arms from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may be able to come from this world to the other of glory. 
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonishments: "Do not undertake any serious illness unless you are called a fool." 
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to III chapters. 
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are of fire cauteries and of medicinal cauteries, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet; and of the forms of instruments, and of the fastenings of the cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work. 
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it orders the chapters and the forms of instruments. 
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is ordered from the head to the feet, and the shapes of the instruments. 
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus as we remember the work, it is fitting that I say the quality of the help and harm of each complexion. 
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest speech and subtlest science and secret answer; and many wise men spoke of these things, and agreed upon them; and their words suffice me little, for I fear the length. 
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, a hot complexion without matter and a dry complexion without matter. 
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complextion together matter, some said and stated that the cautery is a great help; and the others said the opposite: that the cautery is of no use for an illness that comes from heat and dryness. 
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For fire's nature is hot, and it should not be applied to a hot disease by heat, nor dryness; and they who say the opposite, that cautery helps great against hot and dry diseases which come upon men's bodies, 
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold. 
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word. 
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it several times by experience. 
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in every way, do not interfere unless those who have experienced it and know by long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and outcomes, and the space of time; we have no fear of other complexions, even cold and moist diseases. 
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the mire assembled and agreed to the cautery. 
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that the fire cautery together with fire is of the secrets of cures, and of greater benefit than the cautery of burning medicines. 
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come near any member but that which is cooked, and does not harm another member no matter how close it is. 
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines come from one member to another in removing, and bring sickness to the member hindering healing; and by chance it kills the sick person. 
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experience and through the length of my service and study which I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse the length of speech, for it does not please me that I deprive you of the secret which resides in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases from bodies, as the philosopher said in demonstrating; now receive it into your thoughts. 
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what times cauterizations should be done, and they drew up precepts. 
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the following harms are lessened by the help of cautery; and especially if the cauteries are for necessary pains urgent and swift which cannot wait for the time until greater harm comes to the limb. 
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think about it, my son, as foolish men do; for the disease that is healed by cauterization has no return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because cauteries are only a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and worth more than medicine for its haste in its power, and for the virtue of its work and its mastery. 
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the illness and its nature; and superfluous things are gathered in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, if this is not cauterized administered in the place where he has excess superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries of density for pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return at all; but this rarely happens. 
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and that is to see; but they do not believe that cauteries are worthwhile after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures in any illness and they are not effective, then we administer the cautery, and it is effective. 
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then understand well that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish men. 
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries of gold instruments are better than those of iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and the height of its substance; and they said that the burns from a cautery do not cause putrefaction, but that is not true, for I have experienced it and found that it is true in some men; and cauteries of gold are better than those of iron, as they said. 
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And nevertheless when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not cease when it is red due to the color of the gold, and it soon cools down; and if one heats it too much, it melts in the fire; and thus there are enough obstacles. 
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cautery which we have shown to be suitable for our work. 
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered this chapter from head to toe so that the way is easier to find. 
dou cautere olivaire	with olive oil cautery 
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two ways to do it because of a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and the ears, and because of many dreams and toothache, and throat pain, and even for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases. 
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a dissolving medicine, modifying the head III or IV, according to what the strength and illness and the habit of the patient can suffer; and then make the back of the head clean. 
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit crosswise between your hands, and have him place his hands on your thighs; afterward put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers will come, if it bleeds then cauterize with a cautery called "olivare", which has this form: 
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it on the spot marked with ink, and make a descending motion while squeezing your hand bit by bit, twisting; then lift your hand slowly and look at the spot to see if you see the bone just a little; and if you don't see it, start the cautery again until you see the bone as I told you; then take a small piece of silk thread and put in softened cotton inside, and put it on the spot and leave it for three days; then put softened cotton soaked in butter on top; and leave it on until the burn is removed; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And as the ancients said, that when a wound remains open longer, it purges more; and therefore it helps to move it. 
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then cut away what has been burned from the bone, and it should be cured. 
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the cautery should be left on for a long time, and pressed so hard that it lowers the bone as wide as the spindle that women put in their spindles so that the humors can issue out freely; and the wound should be left open for a long time; afterwards it should be cleaned and sutured. 
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem good to me at all, except in some men where there is a way of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them out; for the shoulder is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members; and even when the shoulder of the patient is weak by nature, the first appearance of cautery is safer and milder for me, and from this one I work in consequence altogether for salvation. 
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head 
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the entire head comes chronic pain and lasts long, then the patient should use herbs and pills that are called "cochie", and purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if one does the cautery that we have previously mentioned, it will be of no avail. 
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the head of the patient is strong and not too cold; then cauterize below that cautery a spot as we have said above. 
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you make the cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery where the place is called "vessels" and where we put cupping glasses; and lightly your hand so that you do not see down to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, of which I will speak later; and it is necessary that the cauteries on the horns are finer than those with which we cauterize half of the head, and this is the form.
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head 
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head and the illness extends as far as the eye, and the head is purged by purifying medicines, and other cures have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then make cauteries according to two methods, namely with hot medicine and fire. 
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries of medicine are such that you take a clove of garlic, and remove the skin and cut it into two pieces, and then make a temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can place the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it is placed, bind it well and leave it like that for twelve hours; and then unbind it and put fresh garlic on top, and leave the wound like that for two or three days; then put cotton soaked in butter on top as long as possible. 
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until it is healed; and if you see that you can do this with some burning medicines that I have written or a dose to treat burning medicines. 
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner. 
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery in the following way: 
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "close" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or it has a beak of curvature, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and you put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and twist the fire lightly, as much as half the thickness of the heart is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is behind, and a lot of blood flows. 
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton in the area of the vein, and leave it on for three days; then he puts moistened cotton in butter, and then heals the area with ointment until it is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery which is called "cultellare," at the very tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old. 
de emigraine	from headache 
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a migraine as we have previously described in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries previously mentioned of medicine and iron are not sufficient, then it is necessary that you scarify the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and draw thus upon the painful spot a line half a finger in length, and remove your hand once, and strain so that you do not cut an artery and do not come close to the bone; and beware of the mandible which moves when one chews, and let the nerves have no regard for the movement and let spasms not come to the patient, and beware of the flowing of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting has great fear and itself to him who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced; and leave the work in the middle way; but I will tell you how one restrains blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you the place where it applies in this book. 
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery is not enough for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two knives; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful. 
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of the ears from cold 
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from cold, and one has worked on it with dissolving medicines and other cures as we have said in the division, and the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which this is the form: 
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you point all around the patient's ear, or around both where the pain is held, and remove a bit from its root of the ear after you have marked the place to insert; and put ten points around each ear; then treat the place until it is healed. 
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth 
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cautery is none other than those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make a cautery on those that come from dryness and spasm of nerves. 
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of ailment that moves from phlegm from purging and gargling, and it doesn't work, then it is fitting that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a finger’s breadth beyond the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips; and place the cautery in the part which appears healthy, and make the cautery upon the top of the ear above a finger's breadth below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery on for so long that half of the heart is burned; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the form of the cautery is like the one we have described before, but it is a finger's breadth more subtle and fitting that the knife be a finger's breadth larger; after cure the place as I have said before, until it is healed. 
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not profit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one where it is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and let them be treated as we have said before. 
de litargie	Of lethargy 
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness it is fitting to give the patient large herbs and pills which purify the brain; then raise the head of the patient, and put mustard plaster on the occiput as is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the way of the cautery: if you do so as I have said. 
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy thus, it is good; and if it is not, make three cauteries from the shoulder down to the neck, with two finger widths of space between each cautery; and cure it as the others, and if you see swelling, and the patient suffers, make one cautery in the middle; and if needed, two others on the two horns, and cure until it is healed; and let the cauteries be called "olivare," as I have said before. 
de la froidor dou chief	From the cold of the head 
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of herbs and of what we have said before; after you raise the head of the patient, then make a cautery on the head and on each horn, and the back and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave them until the hottest part is burned, then lift your hand; after you treat it until it is healed, and let the cauteries be called “olivare” which we have said before. 
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy 
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain with herbs and other remedies that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and suffering from a lack of medicine. 
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer it, make him gargle and chew things that modify the brain often with good meats; after he reigns over the head in the middle, and I do the cautery according to what we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffering, I make cauteries as I said to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive according to the manner that I have said. 
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is feverish, do him a subtle cautery according to this method: 
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by reason of melancholy are the superfluities or moist humors corrupted and gross phlegm, then the cautery of parts cauterizes as we have said to him who has paralysis. 
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then let him drink things by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is stated before in the division. 
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After raising the head of the patient; after making a well-made linen twist, as a circle, place it under the head; and have the patient lie crossed, and be well held on all sides; then present the liniment, and mix with butter from old sheep's wool; and heat at a moderate fire so that when you apply it, the patient can bear it; after emptying the circle inside under the head, let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with another good treatment, until he is healed. 
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see that the cauterization is burning too much, make several points with the cautery. 
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery removes the brain cleanly; and then put cotton softened in butter and gelatine fat on top. 
de l’awe des eulz	From the eye of the eels 
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the ill humor first comes as the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and make the patient drink things purifying the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times on an empty stomach. 
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After commanding him to lie on his back, and making a cautery above his head, and making two cauteries above the two temples if the descent of the blood from the brain is at both sides together, or one if the descent is at one side; and cut all the veins and arteries that are beneath the heart, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it as best as you can.  
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incision the caution how you will stretch it; and never make a cautery or haste below the two bones behind. 
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are upon the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it is superfluities cold and phlegmatic, then make the cautery as I said at the beginning of the chapter descending to the eyes: I cauterize on the head, and II cauterize on the II temples, and II cauterize where below the II bones; and if there is more need, I cauterize moderately above the eyebrow with a small cautery. 
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the body of tears by within the eyes 
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not profit, then give the patient three nights of chicken broth; afterwards shave his head, and apply a cautery or half an olive oil cautery; and apply two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two temples, one point below the hair; and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it. 
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called “clavilis”: 
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the membrane of the eye is softened by sickness and moisture, then the cautery of this instrument which is called “olivare”. 
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form: 
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not let go of your hand until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said. 
dou poil qui point l’oil	Where hair points the eye 
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted to red and prick the eye, and one makes cauteries according to two manners: that is to say, of fire or of burning medicine. 
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. 
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are equal, then put the patient in your hand; afterwards trace on paper a figure above the eyes that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then he puts cotton moistened with egg white and plantain mucilage on the eye, then heats the cautery which has this form:  
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked dot by dot many times, so that the flesh is burned at that spot; and the signs of the healthiness of the work are that you see the paper shrink back and the hairs rise up at the point of a needle; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then put cotton softened in butter on it as long as the burn is gone; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs come, and the paper is softened then begin the cautery again on that same spot as you did first; and if the hairs are burned off, cauterize it until the paper is lifted to its natural place and is even, and does not prick the hairs. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medical cautery is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even as possible, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, of each a dram, and grind together well; and do it hastily so that it does not cool, then spread it quickly on the shape that you have made like the myrtle leaf, and put on the paper the eyes; and if the sickness holds in one eye only, so you must work on one, and if on both also; and put under the eye moistened cotton steeped in egg white; and let the patient's head be in your healthy hand and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press the spot and the thumb every time that the patient feels a bite from the medicine, for he will feel a bite as of fire.  
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your hand. 
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite has passed, lift the place where it was, and see if you see the skin raised as if it were raised by fire or by incision; and if it is so, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, put more medicine on the spot where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are set; then put softened cotton in butter until the burning stops, afterwards treat the spot with ointment which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed. 
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to guard yourself well at your work with great care so that no part of the medicine falls into the eyes. 
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin the medicine again on that place which is softened by the paper properly, just as you did before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the form of the myrtle cautery: 
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this are your constraints; and do not be answered the right way by him whose study is of this art. 
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the healing of a fistula by cauterization 
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you burn it according to this manner. 
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place his head on your lap; and hold the ministers' head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or turn its head; afterwards put softened cotton in egg white or juice of parsley on the eye; afterwards heat the cautery which is shaped: and is hollowed at the head just as the shape of a penknife, together with the point; if you see, it should be pointed from one head to the other, and if you see, it should also be like a tent; but nevertheless, that which is hollowed is better for your work. 
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, and treat the rot, and dry it; and if it is closed, do the work, and treat further through the bowels; then put a hot cautery on the form, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part where snow falls above the eye, so that your hands do not shake folly; and put the cautery in the grease of the oil, and corrupt it. 
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the beginning of the cautery to the bone, it would be good. 
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, restart the cautery again and another if you need it, and leave it for 3 days. After that, put softened cotton buttered on it, and cure it with a desiccative ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, put an ague corrosive medicine on it until the bone is uncovered; and follow this according to what he would say in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients said. 
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Open a fistula, and make the place; then put in the opening a subtle thread of which this is the form: 
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the quantity of a 3rd part of lead; and hold your hand or the bandage firmly, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run to his eye; and it is necessary that one puts on the patient's eye moistened cotton soaked in wine or water: the lead heals the place of a fistula, and the healthy flesh by marvelous health. 
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, it is good. 
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a poultice to the nose, and bring the fistula back into the body according to what is appropriate in its proper place. 
des crevaices en levres	of crevices in lips 
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks happen in lips which are called "hairs", and likewise in the lips of children. 
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds of which we have spoken in divisions, and the treatment does not profit, then heat a small surgical cauterizing knife according to this form: 
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly put it into those crevices until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, treat the area with wax until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat 
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes at the root of the throat or in the eye, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after it has decayed and rotted and is old and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after you cut or pierce the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron heats to the bottom of it, and at the last place; and do so once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured this way, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter. 
dou movement des dens	with the movement of teeth 
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and that is not worth it, then put the head of the patient in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery whose shape will come later in this way so that you put a cane on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside hastily, and hold as long as the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and begin the cautery again according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let him keep it for an hour and wash his mouth. 
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is made firm, and the softened gum restrained, and the corrupted moisture dried. 
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of the teeth 
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is coldness or wind, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use a cautery according to two methods: butter cautery and fire cautery. 
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterize with butter is such that you take cow butter and put the end in a spoon of iron or silver; then take cotton and wrap it on the point of a tent peg, and moisten it in melted butter, and put it on the aching tooth hastily and hold it until it cools; and do this often so long as its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that moistened wool and cotton in cold butter and put it on the aching tooth, and put hot iron on it so long as fire comes to the gum of the tooth. 
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauteries with fire are such that you take a piece of iron or wood, and it should be large enough so the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, from which the shape will come afterward, put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled. Do this often, because the pain will be removed that same day or the next. 
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in haste before the cautery, and then quench it quickly; and this is the form of the cautery: 
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery where you wish, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the iron: 
des scrophules	of scrofula 
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of phlegm and cold moisture, and is not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery with hair which afterwards takes the form, and make II openings for the smoke to escape from the cautery on the other side; and place the hot cautery upon the abscess once, or twice where necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for III days; and put soft cotton moistened with butter upon it until the burn is removed; afterwards treat the place with ointments and bandages until it is healed. 
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery: 
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overcomes the channels of the body, and especially when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by dissolving medicines; afterwards you shall cauterize at the root of the throat, and take care not to come near the throat itself, but only burn on the chest, making a single point. 
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you make another cautery at the joint of the neck and the head of the spine, let it be the cauteries which is called "clavile," as we have shown the form beforehand; and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed. 
de la toust	From the cough 
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and sickness of the lungs are of cold humors, and the patient has neither fever nor thirst, and the sickness is old, then make two cauteries on the shoulder blades in their hollows; and the other cautery between the two breasts; and let the cauteries be called "clavile" according to the shape that is mentioned before. 
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see this, make a cautery by pricking with all the cauteries that are called "points" whose shape is shown above in the illness of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or thereabouts. 
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the place according to what has been said before, and let the cautery be three fingers long according to this form: 
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of this, the cauteries are lighter, for you make three at a time. 
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then it is necessary that you first reset the dislocation. 
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After the patient is placed on their back and side; then lift the heart which is inside the armpit with the two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two points like this. 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart as far as it pierces the ribs, and the figure of the cautery would be equal to four cauteries; and for this reason a cautery is made with a cautery that has three points, so that the shape of the cauterization is six cauteries; and the points are according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cautery that has three points: 
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is it applied upon this nerve because there are eight cauteries. 
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After put on the hot cautery bruised with salt; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well comforted. 
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the clavicle, or many cauteries by pricking. 
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed. 
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come to the stomach so that it is drawn out of its complexion, and phlegm is multiplied in it, and accustomed cures are used and they do not profit, then it behoves that the patient be turned onto his back, and extend his legs and arms. 
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Of these then make III cauteries I below the spoon of the foot by the quantity of a coin, to all the cautery clavile, and II cauteries behind the II ribs so that the shape of the cauteries be at III angles, and have equal space between the one and the other so that they are not joined together when they will rot; and let the cauteries be so perfect that they can penetrate the II parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauteries according to this form without adjustment:  
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach one point according to the quantity that you see fit; then cauterize with the whole cautery which is called "points." 
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we have had before, as long as it is healed. 
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver suffers pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is forced out of its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is cured of these things that we have said in divisions, and they do not profit him, then it must be that the patient be purged on his height; and a sign of three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, drawing away from the hypochondriacs, where the ribs of the man come; and have space between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press your hand too hard on all the cautery; and let it be burned only half of the heart, and let the patient be straight on his feet; and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is to cauterize these burns with a knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the whole heart, for you would dry up the whole body; and let it not come to boiling, for the heart is very delicate in that place, and smell to see. 
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too severe; and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain. 
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure deserves the mire, it is fitting that the patient be shaved on his head; and then point to the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a ray, of which this is the form: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the heart is burned and comes to a boil, until the eruption is completely gone; afterwards treat according to the treatment of ulcers until it is healed; and no one should use this cautery except those who have studied long in the art of medicine, by whose hands these diseases have been cured many times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly work, and all the same it seems to me that it is better to leave it. 
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cautery of pleurisy 
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make several cauteries from aristoloche roots, and in this manner: take a long aristoloche root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and also as thick and as long as your arm; and steep it in oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize. One cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and two small cauteries one inch apart descending on the part below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind one inch apart; and one cautery under the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two as for the ribs behind the cautery which is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand at all, but make it openly as if you were smelling. 
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some say that no man should use a fire cautery resembling a razor, heat it, and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and the pain will cease, as we have said in the case of an abscess of the liver. 
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed. 
de la mice	from the mouse
