Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of the mouse according to the divisions of the cures that we have said, and it does not profit, then there are three ways of cautery that are all good. 
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which there is a manner so that you make III cauteries, or IIII, in aligning according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not press your hand at all on the cautery, and let the patient often turn on his back; and another manner of cautery so that you heat the cautery which has II nerves, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is placed near the mouse, or where the cost of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevations which you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After he puts the two inflamed nerves in so that the heart is pierced through from the other side, then draw fire with the cautery, and thus he will have four. And if you see, if he cauterizes all at once with the cautery at three nerves. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has had decay for a long time, this is worth more than the other cures previously mentioned. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not effective for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes." 
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the shoulder, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the thigh, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cauteries be very close to the hopes of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the cautery uncovered for a long time to prevent rot, and do not leave the patient's wound unattended after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be a key as we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been said previously. 
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet 
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is hydropic and they are full of a yellow fluid, it is fitting that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. 
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply with the point, lest you burn the yellow wax, and let the cautery be of this form: 
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making two cauteries on each leg at the point of a knife; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries uncovered for a long time so that it dries out; after curing the other cures that we have said. 
de la menoison	From the mansion 
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any remedies; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, or the circular cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle with all the subtle clavile cautery, and two cauteries on the thighs. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, then cauterize him on the shoulder, and cauterize each vein, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good assistance. 
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids 
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the base, one or several, and they are old and consist of large, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, then apply cauteries: three on the spine of the back, those that are farthest below the almcdate, dot to dot, in a triangle, and one cautery below the elbow; and if you think that his stomach is cold, and the food does not cook, and you see swelling in the face, then apply one large cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with a full cautery. Leave the cauteries open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place so that it is healthy. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul" 
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the athelul, if you heat the cautery which resembles a razor and then put it all ablaze upon the athelul cut; and leave it so long as the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, from which blood will flow; do this one or two times, and if there is much athelul, cauterize each one as we have said; afterward apply beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the athelul, it will be of greater help. 
de plaie mal curee	from a poorly treated wound 
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or incision, which we will describe in their place, then comes a certain illness that can only be healed by cautery. 
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any fistula comes, and is old and has putrid decay and corrupt moisture, you must test its depth with a subtle probe, and make sure that you know the total depth of the probe. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery which resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and restart the cautery until the dead and corrupted flesh is burned once, or two or three times, according to the quantity needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, beware of these wounds, and do not make these incisions except in a fleshy place, and think that it is not dangerous; after healing the wound until it is healed, and if the wound is cleansed, and the matter is removed for a long time, then know that the wound is completely healed; and if the matter is not removed, know that the wound is deep, and the bone rots at the bottom; and as one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	Of the sickness of the kidneys 
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes with heavy winds, and it does not go away despite the woman's efforts, then you must make a cautery on her hips on both sides with the pointed cautery as we have previously said; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, which will do more good. 
de la vessie	of the bladder 
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the back part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, on the right and left, and let each cautery be as long as the nail of a thumb; and make one cautery on the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauteries be sharpened according to the form mentioned above. 
de la marris	of the sea
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marris is cold and moist, and does not allow conception to occur, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are slow; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary that one makes III cauteries around the neck, as we have said of the bladder cautery, and II cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be strong, as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip 
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend to the socket of the hip and for this reason it moves out of place, the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and if two veins are found near the joint, then you should cauterize the patient on the socket of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle, marking in front of the place around the socket as it turns so that the socket is inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach. 
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make three large cauteries from olive wood and let the cauteries be as perfect as all hearts; and cauterize until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip 
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment is ineffective, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After you apply the cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two ways: that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery can be done in many ways, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the thighbone three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and large, and have a space between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on top of the thighbone, so there are four according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cauterizer uses the cautery in a circle as we have previously mentioned for a hip dislocation; but do it in such a way that the circle contains the entire hip, and all the muscle tissue is burned. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg. 
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is holding him, and four cauteries above the ankle, on the left side a mark; and let the cauteries be lancet-shaped, or burn the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, cauterize him where he feels the pain three points or four with the cautery called "points." 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, do more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, apply a cautery with a knife-shaped or circular cautery; and be careful in all your cauteries so as not to leave it long enough to burn the nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient greater pain and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who have performed cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it until the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot. 
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly from which he had death. 
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery in one and the other, according to this manner. 
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said about the cautery of the hip, that this is the manner, make such a tool and let its head be as thick as a nail of a doctor, or a little less, and let it have notches between which there should be space the size of a pea; and let these notches be opposite in two parts and also like knots, and let it have a handle of well-made iron; and this is its form. 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and hot, and then put it on the box of the sick hip, and turn it up on the sound side; and the cauterizer once re-cauterizes it and leaves it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment with anointing until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of the fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; and nevertheless it is one of the good cauteries, for he who can suffer it, and where it applies. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning medical cauteries are made such that you shape the instrument with notches in which the edge of the wound descends, and it is of iron or steel with a long handle, and has two notches at its height, and between each notch the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and they are open above and below, and join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After you place the box of the hip on the patient lying down on his healthy side; then press your hand very firmly on the box of the hip; afterward, put between the two circles of the awl that is heated in the fire for one hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burn. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there is also found a bite as from fire; and when the bites have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the buttock with ointment of sweet awes, and leave it so for three days, and put butter on top until that which is black from the scald is removed; and let it remain for three days so that rot comes out; and this would be the last help after the cure of ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, make the instrument that you have made for the hip in the same way; and this is the manner of the hot iron, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot coals, as much of one as of the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new pot. 
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where it has a small opening so that the point of a razor can enter; and put down one pot over another well-sealed pot, and put alkali and lime and soft water on top, as long as there are two inches of powder until you have it well steeped in your hand; and leave it like that until it runs off clear water and cheese or well-sealed pot, then take all that water and pour it on lime and alkali just as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in the soft works of medicine and in cauteries of other members.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and praised it greatly, and said that no other cure was done, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches it here afterwards. 
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And say in this manner that you take some fresh and dry green litharge and grind it very finely with a little bit of grease, and put it on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain is located, and tie it; and leave it for three hours and according to the amount that the patient no longer feels the burning. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put it in a bath as long as his body is warmed up a bit, and put it in bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of humors. 
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat hair, it helps a lot; and it should be done in this way. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and put it on the joint that is between the thumb and the finger which is called the knuckle. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After you take goat's horn and burn it until it is charcoal, and put it on wool, and leave it until it becomes extinguished. 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back 
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion or by excessive evacuation, or by similar spread of cold matter, none of these conditions warrant cautery except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter. 
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is fitting after the patient has been purged of foul-smelling pills or other such things that they be made on his back where the pain lies, three lines marked with an inch, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery which is called "poin"t; and if you see fit, make three cauteries or four at the medium-sized pointed cautery according to this form: 
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight anus when they rise, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes upon the other spines. 
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it cleansed, if you cauterize it with a cautery according to this form. 
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery evenly scorches each part of the spine. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, that you cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery making II or III lines, and the points are close to one another. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After healing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not apply cautery in any gibbosity that is in a space of nerve.  
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints 
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pains in the joints are from moistures that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the foot, which physicians properly call “gout,” and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary for you to grasp the face of the foot, if you do cautery on all the cautery that we call "point". 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make a cautery on each knee three or four cauteries on each side, with olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand stronger than until the thickness of the heart's core is burned. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knees and back, apply the cautery as we have described in our chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two points around the wrist; and if there is no pain in the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good treatment to the patient and have him take medicines. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed with the help of God. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the face 
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes in the bowels, and the guts descend as far as the groin and it is new, it is fitting that when you see him cleaned, he should not eat anything on that day; and he should use things that loosen the belly so that the bowels descend from his belly. After that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath while the guts are replaced, and reset them at your discretion, and mark down below the rupture on the bone of the hip, and a sign resembling half a circle above the body. Then heat the cautery in this form: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it oozes pus 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and let the assistants hold his hand so that they do not return backwards; work well the thighs of the patient, and put a cushion and a sergeant on the thighs, and another on the foot which holds his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come to the bone; and be careful subtly that the eyeball does not protrude when you are doing the cautery so as not to burn it; and that by this the patient does not die or suffer other harm. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is fitting that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and those for adults be large according to their size; after three days, treat the place of the cautery with butter until the burning is removed; afterwards, treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound heals well; and it is fitting that his bandages be loosened for a long time, so that the pus does not escape when he gets up to go into the rooms. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, let him be given a well-made bandage and wear it for forty other days; and let him have good rest, work little, and guard against too great repletion of drinking and eating, and of crying too loudly; and when he follows this teaching he will be completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of the tailor in his chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly 
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When tumors come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make the cautery hot according to its quantity, and burn one-third of the tumor; afterwards treat according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first sign the place of incision and make a line across its width above the fracture, and another behind it, and hold your hand steady with all the cautery heated. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb 
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help it, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of that one, for such a practice is necessary so that it should change to the member that is closest, so you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed. 
de meselerie	Of a wound 
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The cautery is helped sometimes by great aid, and the same disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you want to cauterize it, be careful if the illness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the ill person, then make five cauterizations on the head: one on the nape, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cauterization reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors from the thick humors can escape; and cauterize according to what is in front. 
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the measles is scattered all over; and it clearly wanes, it is fitting that you cauterize it with these cauters that we have said or chief, and one cautery on the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttocks and another nearby, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the wrists, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the last bone of the heel, so that you do not burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when you do more cautery, you do more help and move the profit; and know that the sick do not feel any pain from the cautery as the healthy feel it, because the body is already completely corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the wound with flour of vetch mixed with honey and other cures until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any limb and is healed by medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not cured, then make cauteries on the limb according to the size of the limb; and let the cautery be a small puncture penetrating into the thickness of the flesh; then heal it with ointments until it is cured. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And it is sometimes done with the cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; and nonetheless no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.  
de albaras	From alabaster 
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness which is called “albaras” has become old, and the remedies of medicine are of no value, then cauterize with a cautery a perfect spot, according to the quantity of the species of the heart, so that the whiteness be removed, and its color be changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of pigeon and blood of almond, of each one part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it at the place until it is healed. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of ulcers by cautery 
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears, and you see it stopping, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the chancre. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nevertheless, the surgeons say that one should also apply a cautery in the middle of the ulcer; and nevertheless, it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and moreover, what is right is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called “circle,” as we have said in the chapter of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move 
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it lingers to die either due to the superfluity it causes or due to the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and has little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then let the cauterizer surround with many small cauterizations by pricking; afterwards leave it thus. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce all the way through with the cautery, heat the cautery so that it is this shape: 
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that ailment which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it behind in some way so that the course of the rot is alleviated. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment as long as it is perfectly healed. 
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron 
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another kind of illness which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a wasting away of the limbs, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry twigs. 
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can endure the heat of fire together, then heat small and large cauteries according to what suits the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize all around so that you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply cauterized softened wool with oil on top until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption. 
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the healing of wounds generating flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, apply the cautery again to that which remains from its place corrupted. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ailment has sometimes been cured by a sharp blade in place of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure with a sharp blade in the division: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the leeches which come to the feet 
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that at the feet through fire a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding and is a large thing lacking which bleeds the foot. 
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this illness are according to two manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot iron cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery like a quill feather and make it from good iron so that it can penetrate the nail on all sides and has subtle edges; then place it red-hot upon the nail and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for III days until it begins to rot; then make a plaster of wild mallows bruised with salt, and leave the plaster upon it all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place of ointment spreading charcoal until it is healed. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire on the body, and often happens in hands and feet, it is necessary that you apply a hot cautery; and it is done this way: take a cane of iron or wood, or a feather quill, and put it on the wart and the nail, that is to say, for warts and boils; and put the cane on so that it encompasses all around, then put a piece of red-hot iron on top, and hold your hand well and press it while turning it so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the wart, and can find the hot iron going deep down to the root; let the patient endure the bite of the hot iron for an hour; then leave it like this and it will uproot all its roots.  
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do one after another, until you have pulled out all those that are in the body, then heal the inflammations which breed flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling 
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold of nerves, or from quartan fever or other, it is fitting that you make him four cauteries or four on the spine of his back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on his foot, and one on his stomach with an olive cautery; he will stop trembling, and hasten the health from the cold sickness. 
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules 
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes ulcers appear on the body, or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted substances. 
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is fitting that when they appear at first we make a cautery on each head of the pustule; 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never do they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further forward, but the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and are healed; but it is fitting that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut 
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes after the cautery, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to staunch. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And in any case when this happens, if you hurry to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it very hard until the blood is calmed down under your finger, and no more drops; then heat several small and large cauteries with olive oil until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is severed, and put the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire. 
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do one after the other until the blood is stemmed; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be properly stopped if the artery is large, unless this is done by one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by a strong ligature of thread, or by medicines placed upon which have the power to stop blood; and it should be tied and strained tightly. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will apply ligatures tightly with bandages or put burning things on it, or other similar things, it will not be profitable and will do harm.  
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no mirror or medicine present, they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press well until it rests upon the wound and upon the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water often, so that it is very cold, until the blood is frozen and thickens and rests; and make inquiries beforehand about those who need cauteries and medicines. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures of the side 
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is fitting to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, and the ointments and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have put this chapter from the head down to the foot, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that one can more easily find what one wants. 
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this one, it is fitting, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than the first one of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution. 
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there often occurs the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. 
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment. 
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If some come who torment themselves so much with their illness that they die easily because of the severity they find in their illness, and the intensity of its malice; and these one must fear. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And some of these give you their meaning and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is malicious. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not work foolishly but wisely from those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can take lessons; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your patients to which health is converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and long memory. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen. 
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have ordered this chapter in divisions by chapters, according to what it is before this chapter of cauteries, that I have divided from the head to the feet so that you may find more easily what you will need. 
dou chief plein d’aigue	sharp head full of pain 
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the child's head too hard; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and all those that I saw hastened death; and for this it seems to me better to leave the work on these cures. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was full of pain, and his head grew larger each day until he could no longer support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture gathered below the bone on the shoulder blade, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you split open the head with a wide incision; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture can run out; and see here the shape of the spatula: 
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker and the abscess larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross like this: 
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs you see are the corners of the head open on each side, and a sharp jump occurs when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not respond to you: then it is fitting that you split the top in three incisions according to this manner: 
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture. 
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After removing the dressings of cloths and powders, he puts wine and oil on it, and leaves it like that until the fifth day; then he unties it, and cures the wound with bandages and ointments, and leaves the head bound equally, and gives the patient dry meat free from moisture to eat so that the limb may be strengthened and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and the gathering of the point; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the abscess opens, and empty it of the sharp matter, and the wound according to what you are able to do; and take care not to sever an artery; and let blood flow so that the patient does not die from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	Of rheumatism 
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or breasts, and the illness is old, and medicine does not help at all, then the last resort is cautery with which one sears the two arteries. 
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then, when you see them swollen, that the patient bends his head back; after rubbing the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then remove the patient's collar with the whole cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the veins of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are filled; then mark the veins in an incision, then cut both of them with a sharp spathula of two parts, until the size vein reaches the bone, and this should be done across the width of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatula under the artery and the cup above, cutting as much as it should through. 
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if the blood flows continuously upwards. 
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, it is fitting that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then sign a line and cut until the bone; and what it is fitting for blood to put out is six ounces, and perhaps one drop more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains upon the bone point without suppuration, if the pus that forms abscesses does not come there, then strain the wound and bind it, and apply ointment dressing until it is healed. 
de emigrainne	from emigration 
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes and acute catarrh, due to moisture from tears and the heat in the temples, and old head pain and similar things, and it is treated by medicinal remedies and all that does not profit him, then we should extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have told. 
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is this: the patient should pull back the hairs from his temples, and listen for the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is less full outside than in some men who are too cold; and if it is full, he should bind his neck with some cloths, then rub the place with some coarse cloth, and raise the place with hot water so that the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula which has this shape: 
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then lift it up with forceps and carefully remove all the webs that are beneath it from each side; and if the artery is delicate, turn it at the point of a hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two ends. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not copied, so will it not jump at all without doubt altogether. 
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain the blood from the sixth hour to the third; and if the artery is large, it behooves you to tie it in two places with a strong doubled silk thread, so that putrefaction does not come before the suturing of the wound, and blood flows; then cut away the excess which is between the two ties at that same hour; and then, if you see fit, cauterize with a scalpel cautery down to the bone until the flesh is cut; and this is a milder operation, if the patient does not have a fever and he is of a hot complexion. 
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery is helpful to end humidities, for which it is of greatest help against humidities. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one must fill the place with old cotton and put well-made tents on top; and when they are untied, let it be treated with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if there is a lack of artery in as much as you work, hurry to cauterize it, or apply vitriol to the place and hold it with your hand until the blood is stopped; and if you don't have this present, put your finger on the place until the blood is frozen, and lift the place from sharp cold until the blood ceases, and it will be extracted as necessary; and he who is more skilled and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this trenchant cautery of two parts, but let the trenchants be well spaced to keep their heat longer.  
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less. 
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two knives a space of one fist's width, and then when you have marked to incise the two sides, and you place the hot iron on top until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two sides; and they are separated between the two edges because it is not soldered with this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery: 
des larmes	of tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes descend along the veins that are above the bone of the head, and no medicine cures it, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and his forehead throbbing as if with shivering; and if they are strained and moist so that the hairs on the papers are falling out, and the papers are scalded and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary.
