Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in ancient times "cure contuse", and you must do to the patient who has this ailment the hairs on his forehead, then make three cuts on his forehead equally according to the length of his forehead; and let one of the cuts be as long as two fingers all down along the forehead until the nose, and the other two as two ribs above the temples; and beware of cutting into the arteries that are at the two sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and each wound should be three fingers wide at its crossing; and have ready a piece of sponge and plenty of cloths for wiping up the blood, then put the spatula sharpened on both sides which has this shape: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is behind the temple to the second incision; and flay all the heart which is between the two fissures at its entire thickness which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract therefrom this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first fissure, which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, it has this shape: 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp side towards the flesh burned at the heart, and the dull side toward the bone, and push until it comes to the middle fissure. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to those as far as the incision is continuous until it opens to the heart, and then make another cut in the middle fissure until the other defurcation; and then draw out the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton in each fissure, and put soft cloths moistened with wine and oil and alum on top, and guard against boils arising there; and on the third day untie the ligature, and he applies a large poultice of hot water, then cure it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	where rheumatism of the eyes 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some acute catarrh comes habitually, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakens the sight, and burns papers; and the hair falls out, and when someone in pain has a headache, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that these humors and this phlegm come from many veins, and the cure for it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And command the patient to hold his forehead, then make a large incision between the eyebrows, and another two fingers wide. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone; and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples which move in eating; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then sever between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then bind over it cloths softened in wine and oil, and beware of a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until the flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying things which cause charring. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour flowers, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and administer it to these wounds to generate flesh throughout. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	For the removal of ears 
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that lodges in the ears is one of four things: either grains, or an animal, or a stone from a mine or a similar thing like iron; or seed, such as barley, beans, peas; or something flowing like water and easily like it and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or something else that doesn't fit in the ear lodges there, and it doesn't grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, and it secretes any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze by command, and he plugs his nostrils when sneezing comes, and puts around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear on top. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times force comes by this cure; and if it does not come by force, administer its extraction with subtle pincers, of which here is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the forceps, that's good; if not, perform extraction with a fine needle of small gauge; and if it doesn't jump out that way, make a cane of iron and push the head of the cane or the hole of the ear hard, and fill that which is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane; then pull firmly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in any of these ways, take some glue like that used to catch birds, and put a little on any instrument suitable for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull firmly. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump out from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear as in abscesses, boils, and spasms; and the manner of the incision is that you first lance the patient on the head, and draw out blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it depends on the fat; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, until you reach the bone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is within and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin spatula subtly according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist due to moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces from it; then extract it with subtle pincers and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is smooth. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute pain then when the jaw is inflamed in the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a sneezing of condition first and amples the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the pain is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps further than that, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and warm them a little in the fire; then place one or two openings of his ear on them, and hold it so with your feet on the other side, and strike another stone upon the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease to do this from stone to stone until all the pain is gone, and thus will it all go away. And if you see that it needs it, take a piece of iron and heat one of its ends in the fire, and the other end hold in your hand so that the hottest piece of iron burns; then redo it with other pieces of iron until all the pain is gone as we have said for the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of a beast, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body so that one can feel it, then administer extraction with pincers; and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if after you have cured them as we have said in the section on treating distillations, and the cure does not help at all, then look at the ear in the sunlight. If you see any worms, remove them with fine tweezers. And if you do not see any, take a cane shaped like this: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the finest tip in the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suck all the way out the vein; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, then stuff cotton around the worm like I have said for the stone; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them or treat the distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, whose form is like you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it be of silver or iron, three holes are made beneath the small openings, and above there is a cover for distilling; and to press within the distillation an instrument of iron well made for this purpose; and if you wish, take the razor and wrap around the point with cotton well moistened; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the tube, and let the tube be in the ear; then put the whole cotton into the razor, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or has reached the ear; and the patient feels it within, and let the distillation be somewhat warmed by the fire, thus one distills it in the ear; and see that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of the ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to men by a tearing of a wound, or by a splinter driven into the ear, and this tearing sometimes comes perfectly into the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes there appears a hole that burns the opening, and one sees it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes in by way of perfection, if one cannot see it, is a healing ailment of many positions, and in this case one sees that you must put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see an apparent eruption, if the work has had all these sorts of things from which this form arises. 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and cutting in front and behind all the way through, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opilation is of flesh or cartilage of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and cut lightly, until the said flesh is entirely removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is perfect in the ear, then take a subtle and light razor and heat it a little in the fire, then put it on the body of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the swelling where the patient has pain in the ear, pierce lightly and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a tent into the ear according to the width of the hole, and soak it in Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do this at any time, for as long as the wound is sutured. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood comes, immerse a sponge and cloths in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the flow of blood which are found in treatises on distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papers 
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This tool which comes in papers from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is fitting that you extend them with forceps and pincers, and the stalk of a spatula from its roots; then put on the place ground vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without cutting, the cautery uses a lentil-shaped subtle cautery, and after incision it is able to move; and many times they heal, when nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return. 
de la gresle	From gravel 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come on the skin certain things that seem rough in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of moisture thick on the skin above and below; the work is such: take care if the grandine moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know; do so make a large incision, then lightly scrape the skin from each side, then take hold of it with pincers, and cut it off. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing a little bit of the paper, do not grieve at all for the patient; and if the tear is large, assemble it with a stitch, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, because ointments will restore it quickly and produce flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone descends into the ear towards the upper part, then turn over the paper and grasp the hailstone with tweezers, and cut and press it on one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter; and when the hailstone is cut, pour oil of sharp salt and cure the place from which it originated as long as the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is smeared on cloths of paper above it, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it grieves much in their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears rush into their eyes; and because of this they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep upon them, and have their papers moist beneath their eyebrows so that they swell, and their appearance is covered with exinach which appears in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exirnach between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient puts his head in clean water; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity which contains pus from each part, then put it on him; and press with your two hands on one side and the other, so that the pus gathers within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at a sharp spatula a slit two fingers wide, and it should not be larger than the wound one makes when opening a vein; and make the skin whole as much as you come to the pus; and in several positions pus comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat. 
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove then the whole piece of cloth between your fingers at the fire, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not add to the split, lest you come to all the spatula up to the eye, lest you bruise it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the arrowhead does not appear at the beginning of the incision, widen the incision slightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the site, and bind tightly. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then let the healer apply soothing plasters until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper  
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the eyelids which are not natural, and they are aged, they are harmful to them, and they bring about kinds of illnesses such as accustomed tears and softening of the eyelids and albugine, as long as it is a cause of the destruction of them; and the cure is according to four manners: either by cautery together with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by canes, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if you put a needle all along it above; and let this be below the margin of the paper or where the hairs grow below these hairs, and draw the thread above the whole paper, and turn it at the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs added, to the whole spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small one; then remove the thread, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then sign on the paper a figure of an anchor, as the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided into all. 
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is someone who needs a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make at all the spatumile upon the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear up to the small one; and let one of the clefts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the lancet into one of the two angles of the heart, then flay it all; then bring together the two lips with a stitch of an needle at all one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the superfluity of the threads dry upon the two eyebrows without any gluey things, if you see how to do this; and if not, have no care, then leave the stitch and the threads until three days or four; then treat the wound without a stitch with drying and constricting things, for the paper will revive at the healing of the wound and the bringing together of it, but the stitch is useless (as the ancients say), and this work is without fear; and if there is another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have said, at three lancets detached according to the shape which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then bind those who overcome small forces equally according to the shape which is here: 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with thread, and put it in the shape; and put one thread near the large tear duct, and the second thread near the small one, and gather between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have said, then bring together the two edges of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs on the paper are converted: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canes is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and put the end inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of a spoon; and take two ends of two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what rises from the oil of the paper, and strain the two canes of the two parts form; and leave it like this for several days, and the skin that is strained will die and heal and carry, as long as it seeks by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, so the cautery has some force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound closes, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the two cautery marks that you will make according to this shape, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a subtle needle, and put the thread of silk soft and subtle through it; then assemble the ends and tie one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the chase the other subtle thread of silk quickly, and tie the heads of the two threads; then put the patient's head in your healthy hand; and let it be below the sun so that the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and small work, then put the needle at all the chase at the root of the hair next to it, and make it pierce the paper hastily as you draw it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull out your hand so that the hairs come out at all the chase in the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the arrowhead is removed and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the arrowhead below all the thread that you have ordered upon it until the arrowhead comes out completely through the hole above it and you see it by the sight of your eye; then you will treat the arrowhead and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for II days or III, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows up over it; and if the hairs are small, you will accompany them with one long horsehair that is natural, and let it be raised with the one that you leave there, until it is elongated and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rotting of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacratio" or putrefaction comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs through the cutting of a wound, or by incision or cautery, and by similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of working on it is that you split that suture and separate the lips of it, and put linen tents inside, and bind it as long as it heals; and it is not fitting that you use in its care things that dry and constrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first; but work from softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or ale and flaxseed are cooked, and ointments of diascordium melted in any of the oils, and it wraps a tent, and cures it. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you take care that it does not heal according to the form that it was before; and this work that we have said is no other than directions for this ailment so that it does not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness which is below, which truly is called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and lacerations and cauteries and similar things; and the way to work it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and put it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct as far as the right, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then spread the flesh above all the needle, and cut it at a span wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side within the paper; and let the heads of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision you have made, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter that has the Greek letter “I”; then remove that flesh according to the amount its sides are affected below, from that which follows the paper, then join the two detached parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then apply the cure that we have said of softening medicines and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, it is fitting that you make a full fissure below the hairs of the skin, and according to what has been said before; then cut between the two edges of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare themselves with all their power on how to make the shape return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what it is fitting for him in terms of work and instruments has several dispositions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	with the pounding of paper 
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of an egg, and it cannot move or do its natural work, then you must put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and take it with forceps, as much as what is aerated by a very subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too trenchant, so that the patient may not suffer from the spatula being too sharp or that the oil becomes bleared; and let your incision, by which you flay the assembled one, be lightly made, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all that assembly is healed, and do it sometimes in salted lye, and lift it with sweet lye and with colander; then put between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put wool soaked in plenty of egg yolk on the oil; and after the third day use lukewarm water and things that are boiled down as much as it is healed.  
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the corner of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: one is nervous and resembling hard fat, and another which is not nervous but resembling white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and thought to be pinched, cannot be grasped; and both of these appearances begin towards the great tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is such that the patient puts his head in sound health, then he works the eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then coil the nail as pincers of small doubleure, and extend it above; then take a needle, and put a hair of horse, or cow, or ox, and thread strong; and double the point of the needle a bit and stick it within the nail, and pierce it through the whole needle, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it above, and flay all along the hair the side of the nail which touches the prune and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut off the remaining in the root of the tear gland throughout the whole spatula subtle and with small forces, and leave the flesh natural or tear gland, so that through the incision does not come the body's accustomed tears; and sometimes extend the nail to the oncine only, and to the thread, as we have said; then the flay one has throughout the whole spatula smooth of which this is the form: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the prune is not pierced; and after the incision put into the eye a piece of silk thread, and with a collar made of silver, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle and the pliers cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured by medicines; as I have said in the division and if you see it covered, do the eye of the patient and take a small spatula lightly sharpened according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the splinter subtly, and if you see that it diminishes nothing and the rasping urges it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red lead and just crushed, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same operation, as long as it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing else is against it in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it and first heal the hot abscess until it is healed, then start the work as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh near the eye is harmed by excessive tears, suspend it with a thread and cut off part of it, but not all at once so that the flow of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows upon the pupil 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men, red flesh never grows at all, and it covers the prune and draws back on papers and turns them to ashes, and it seems like a rose of bristle; and the works are such that the patients puts his head in a healthy place, then he performs the flesh, and with all that flesh, one must put suitable cauteries for those, and hold them firm; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting all with a razor to the end, and be careful not to blind the eye during the work; and let the incision be from the spatula as we have said in the incision of the fingernail and with little forces by which one removes the pus, as the form after this chapter shows; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply oil of sealwort where you distill red colander and similar corrosive medicines, and put hot cotton over the eye with yolk of egg so that it may be well secured against a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the without pain overcomes you, and you doubt a hot abscess, leave the eye and cure the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and do so for as many flesh are added to the eye by this resemblance. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in any case, it is necessary that you relieve the treatment of each one weak from the natural way; and from the accidental way, by work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb can withstand this work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red ones that are covered on top of the eye, and endure in sight their work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary then first that you look at whether the oil, in which it resides, is strong and there is no other disease except the sebum; then treat the oil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins at all their ends according to his skill, and let the ends be subtle double according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be applied by degrees in the body according to this form: 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one must coil the veins subtly and wipe away the blood hour after hour until you see the veins move away from the eye; and be careful that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut away anything but the veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red colire to corrupt what remains under the eyelid. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot remove all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the eye with soothing things for pain, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and the hot abscess is sure, then start again according to this manner that is above until it is healed; and this is the form of forces: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then you must cut into the abscess where it should dwell and drain all the moisture there until the bone is exposed.  
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the king has all the instruments of which this is the form; and it is called "sharp head," and it is made of hard iron at the head point, and it is pointed like a file as it is in the present form: 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is gone; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the fistula is soldered, and flesh grows, and the body of the bowel is soldered, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not abscessed, and no bad accident comes to it, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, there is nothing else to do but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this method: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with an iron, and with sharp medicines; and when it is uncovered, take a drill according to this method, and let the head of the iron have three angles, and let the bit be thinned down to the point as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and remove your hand from the eye until you can see, then return to drilling the entire hole until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the vein in it stops. 
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens completely and there is no disturbance in the eyelid, or lessening, then you must bind the patient; then cleanse it, then apply cupping glasses or a cautery without cutting to draw out blood, then place on the eye a plaster made of acacia, aloe, frankincense, and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye and put the plaster on top of bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity the eye needs; then bind it over with a hard bandage, and repeat the cupping glasses to draw out blood without cutting; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the strained eye day and night, and if the plaster loosens, you must strain it more; then remove the plaster after a day and a night, and if you see the eye recover, it is good; if not; repeat the plaster and cloths and the plaster and the cupping glasses until it is healed.  
dou derrompement de toile uvee	For a rupture of cloth with a warp
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, and it appears open, and there are tears like resin grains, and it is apparent to see; then if you see it split, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then thrust another needle where it has double thread from the part of the tear; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its arrangement; then grasp the place of the double thread and tie one part of the warp around it, and pull it well, then extract the needle and put a piece of linen soaked in plenty of egg white on top of it; and leave it until the threads knit with the warp, then cure the area with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at no time is the wound restricted by the warp on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a large appearance, pierce it with a fine needle that comes out perfectly from the other side, and drain the white moisture and draw out the eye, and let it heal quickly; then extract it while it is healthy. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bowel of the eye 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bowel that is assembled in the eye, resembling descending fire, and it is not fire; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it as much as you see the bowel coming up to your eyes; then let it be fixed, and do not descend and let it be unburdened with light, and see the things the patient usually sees; and if it does not descend below, know that it is fire, and if the descent of the bowel is not even as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and cut on the corneal membrane I poke through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the crown, until the bow rises; and when it has risen, distill in sharp hot oil mixed with honey, or sharp water where fenugreek is boiled and honey, then let it be healed with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	sharp objects of the eye 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of needles in division, and what it is necessary to pierce; so work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is on the left, or in your right hand if the eye is on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is on the left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is on the right; then put the point of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a ray in that whiteness of the eye at the part where the smaller tear duct is; then push the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the "almagda" comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the "almagda" way be at the perfect measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal veil, then put the instrument until where the point is, then express it below one way after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the point is now lowered, let the patient see it in front of him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if the sharp object goes up the second passageway, place force on it with an instrument. And when it is stuck in and it does not rise, carefully remove the almond slightly while turning your hand bit by bit; then put in again a little piece of silk thread, and lift the eye from within. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a cloth soaked in rose oil or linen softened in plenty of egg yolk and bind with good oil. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on a common poultice with plenty of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyelids too hard, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit," of which this is the form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle place, then insert almond paste, as we have said; and for the completion of the work prepare the patient by having the doctor approaching while he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be devoid of all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition up to the third day; then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is fitting that you delay this, because the pain rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess appears, untie the eye before the seventh day and apply what soothes the abscess; and when it is appeased, untie the bandage and put on its face a piece of orilliet to cover it for a day, and keep it in that darkened room. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he leaves the house little by little, and converts back to his former state; and know that no disciples should interfere in this matter. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his land they made an almond-like thing, by which one sucked the sharp point [of a needle], but nonetheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they shall be properly of iron. 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of these same instruments be of such subtlety, and the last one in three sharp angles. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose 
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or grow various fleshy growths, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and if there are such that have a flesh colored red, and some flesh colored white. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those cases of these humors which are soft and not hardened, it is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work his nostrils and pour the oil into those humors, and draw them out with force; then cut what you can grasp with a fine sharp spatula on one side, as long as you know that this humor is completely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be removed, use all the surgical instruments subtly and lightly so that nothing remains; and without straining yourself, or an abscess becomes swollen, cut it as is necessary; and for malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize it until the pus dries up and all the matter is removed, then pour wine mixed with vinegar. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the newborn's work, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh near the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then it behooves you to put a linen thread, a bit thick, and knotted by hand, and have between each knot a space of a third or less; and put the newborn's cheek on the thread in its nose at its lowest part, and pull while smelling so that it comes through the nose into the mouth; and often children are done this way at schools, and it is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as they are on the thread.  
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the flesh has become corrupted, then draw the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nostril just as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put a cane of lead in the nostril for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, to which one distills oils and medicines into the nostril:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it is of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and you lead it so; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle at the head to hold it when you heat the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh out of the nose 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
