Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head, and it grows and becomes large until it is a visible thing to behold; and for this reason, you must cut it at the beginning and remove all of the bone, then put the cautery or burning medicine on the place; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, be careful if it is hard, of dark color, of poor feeling: do not touch it with iron for it is an enchanted abscess; because when one cuts it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that one can cut it all, then empty the patient and cut without fear, and cure the place with drying and restraining things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilaginous operations, it profits little, except in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then when this happens to anyone, if you see that the wound is fresh and bleeding; then bring the two edges together in a suture, then heal it until it is healthy; and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, then you must scrape all the parts of their core until they bleed, then join the two edges together in a suture, and remove it, and powder with dragon's blood powder and ground incense; and put a piece of strong plaster or another soldering plaster on the powders, and leave it until it discharges by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is healthy. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is such that you bring the edges together: either with needles, as we have said in stitching the belly; or with thread, as I have shown you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When homes appear inside the lips, hard abscesses resembling grains of rye, small and large; then you must turn back the lip, and split open each one, and take them with pincers and cut in each part; then apply to the place after the incision vitriol powder, until the blood is stopped; and then a poultice of flax, and heal the place with dry things until it is healthy. 
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run out; then put vitriol powder, or other restraining and drying powders on the area; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gatherings at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and citrine and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so it is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaw be in your lap, and raise the teeth where the scabs appear, until there is nothing left; and do this for the blackness and the greenery, and for the jaundice and other stains, until they are cleansed; and if one removes what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, begin again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments to raise, according to what the work shows, because the razor with which one raises the teeth has other forms than those with which one raises between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is fitting when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay the pulling as much as you can, for this one must not do; for it is a very high substance until which we have no excuse for the pulling. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to draw, it is fitting that you are certain of the tooth pulling. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks that it is from a bad tooth, and he has the good tooth pulled; and nevertheless the pain does not depart because of this, as long as the evil remains, for we have often wanted to do this to these saints; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then it behooves you to scrape around the tooth at every point with a spatula strong enough to hold back the gum from all sides; then move it towards your hands or with subtle forceps at the first stroke and stroke, until it is well loosened, then affirm the forceps well; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold him firmly so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take any of these instruments and gently insert it into each side, and move it as you did at first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and gnawed, it behoves you to fill it with cloths, where the holes are; and if you extract it subtly with pincers, so that it does not break when extracted; and it is very wise to work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and the patient suffers greater pain from the root's malice than before. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not do as the ignorant surgeons do, who by their haste and boldness often break the bone, and do not bring about what we have said; but they often bring a greater disease by the roots that remain, or by the bone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the bone is dense, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if discharge of blood comes, which often happens, then apply the powder of vitriol; and if this does not work, then cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments with which one pulls the teeth first should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are their shapes: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large members so that they do not bend in the opposite direction, and made of well-made iron, and have teeth to hold the pieces. 
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, it is fitting that you put on the place cotton moistened with butter for one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the sinews are softened, then insert the pliers which are called “algefri,” so that the head resembles a beak of a bird; and they should be made inside as with a file, and this is its shape: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a small scraper, of which this is the form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out because of this, it is good; if not, help yourself with all the instruments, from which the forms will come hereafter: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two arms, of which this is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are before in the manner of teeth, and of this instrument which seems like large pincers, whose form is this: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments are dense; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master artificers find by themselves their own instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of others, so that it does not break a chariot or other bones, or it rots, if he seeks the instruments that suit it, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which here is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-gripping to hold the bone so it doesn't escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, you can remove it with all these instruments. 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course of the body, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the gum is born after the tooth and is not in its right place, and cannot be treated or filed; then use a rasp. If it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument which has this shape and resembles a small beak, made of sharp steel at the end: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the saw cuts little by little in the hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears one can file it, then the file of a part files as here is its form: 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth little by little in your hand lightly so that it does not move until it falls out; then smooth it at the end with no rasp at all, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then you must file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loose, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they are chewing without it hurting, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and that does not work; then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes; let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you see that you can align the teeth, take the thread and wrap it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose tooth/teeth between them, if there is one or several, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then start over with the wrapping until the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and gently so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the head of the bone with forceps and assemble them, and put it between healthy teeth, so that it does not bite the tongue; and then leave it tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens or the threads break, remove it with another thread; if it remains and serves in this way throughout its time, it is the form of the teeth and the shape of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two missing ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth chips, if you put it back in its place, again and again, as we have said; and do not interfere with anyone who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes make a shape of a cow's bone tooth, and put it in the place where the defect is, and extract it as we have said, and it will last and serve for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To loosen the ligament of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament which comes under the tongue, either by nature or by accident of a sewn wound, appears.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood flows from it, put ground vitriol on the spot; and if it does not stop, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it is of a dark color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is leaning towards whiteness, and there is moisture, then cut the skin, and make a small incision with a fine spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the pain goes away from your work, put crushed vitriol on it until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the pus; then lift the place of the wound from pressure and swelling, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes a boil comes inside the throat that are called "godath," and they are properly called the two almonds; when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it at all with iron, so as to avoid the discharge of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will cut it, or it will break on its own; and if it is of a white color and the root is slender, have your instrument ready to cut, but first look to see if the abscess is warm and at rest. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and let his arms be stretched out straight, and open the mouth and take the instrument between your hands, and press the tongue down below the whole instrument; and it should be made of silver or refined steel just like a knife. 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Hold your tongue against all these instruments, and you see the abscess; then take the lancet and put it in the almond (of the abscess), and pull strongly above as much as you can; and do not draw anything from the cloths with it; then cover the instrument, by which this form is made, which seems like one force; but all its heads are curved, and one against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of hardened iron or steel. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, take tongs, of which this is the form: 
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner; and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, both hot and mild, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water, or cooked pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves and similar things until the blood is stopped. Then cure it until it heals; and if at any time other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them similarly as the two almonds are cut. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, to be precise, an abscess of a small size; and it had almost completely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained like this for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that he had to put two reins through the two holes of the nose. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hasten then quickly, and put in one an incision, then the wound was large, and I took a great portion of bowel; then I did another in the other orifice of the nose, and opened its mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I put the incision in these abscesses, and extracted some pus, and only a little blood came out; and thus was unstopped the conduit of the throat for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I lanced it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards. 
de l’uve	of the eye 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below large and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the pus from the abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and the one which is round gathered together and is not long; and it is bloody or of a yellow color or black, then you must avoid cutting into it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger upon the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it according to the manner that I have said of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument which we mentioned before; then insert the awl into the eye, and draw it down below, and grasp it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned for the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut away more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut away more, it grieves the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and care for it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of being cut, you should give him something to dull the fear of the cautery. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and pointed. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patient place his head in sound health, and then press his tongue to the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and bind it with a sharp, fine thread, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and employ the end of this instrument, of which form is as follows: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And say or place a hair where one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine inside so that it does not descend to the throat and the bleary; then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it on the eye, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it shrink and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument with all the cotton into the cane above, as long as the cotton heats up on the eye; and do this often, as long as the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and cut after four days or five. And if you need to start the cautery of the medicine again, start it again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and let it be washed with cold water and be cured with gargles until it is healthy. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and wormwood and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them in a pot, and put them in, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument fixed according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it be of silver or iron, and let one of the heads be thrust into the patient's mouth as far as the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is mortified; then repeat often, until the eye dries up, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the arrival of a hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head a crust of egg, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the crust of egg does not make the vapor weigh down on the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether healthy. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fishbone or something else lodges in the throat. So it is necessary that you draw out what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all your instruments so that you see the thing move; and that which does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it extracts the thing by vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge or a piece of navel or a root of lettuce or a piece of stale bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it arrives at the place, it will detach, then you will draw it out with force; and if it does not come out with what we have said, take an instrument of a plumb according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be bent at the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted up high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it closes on you, nor push any bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument in, because he knows where the thing is airy; if it goes down, or he pulls it out forcefully with the whole instrument equally, as long as it is loose. 
de la sansue de la gorge	From the bloodletting of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is enough, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look into the throat of the sick person towards the sun, then press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, cut it with very small forceps or with subtle tongs that are suitable for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hollow reed, and put it into the throat of the patient, then put the end of the reed on a hot iron, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And hold the patient with sharp pain every day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full vial of cold water and work the mouth open and let it swallow down the whole length, and move it about often with its hand; and as soon as the flesh feels the cold, it will fall away. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will fall without delay. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are hot coals, and let it be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that hole put the head of the instrument; then he pours his fumigation, and the patient puts the top of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes up to the nostrils; and the nostrils will now discharge, and if they do not, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient have thirst, and eat salty things and such, and drink no water; and then it is necessary for her to discharge through this treatment. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats a fistula is, when one can see it, like tongs bent to enter into the throat; and has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has the roughness of a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; and see here the form: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses are similar, according to the recollection that follows here and there in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and they are of two kinds, one of which is in its appearance itself, and the other from the moisture it contains. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those wounds which are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the buttocks, and abscesses of fleshy areas are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the belly is ripe according to its fulfillment; and if there are such that it behoves to pierce when they are mature, and do not die according to their fulfillment, such as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is rotten around, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, by which there is a cause for contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will injure the principal limb; where it is near the fundament, perforate it even when it is dead; and it is not fitting that you perforate an abscess crude without digestion being completed, except for that which is near the fundament, lest it rot thoroughly, and be lengthened within, and a fistula arise; and it cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion; and it is when the pain is calmed, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and from the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where there is more dependence of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the perforation be long according to the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equals where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the member which is bent. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy place, it is best that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of this, the body will be elongated with venom from it, and is full of much filth; and by chance the lips harden and its depth. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small openings, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it has become as yellow as a drape, and is mortified, then it is necessary to do as one does with boils: and if there are some that are split into three angles, and if there are some that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of angers; and if there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, it is fitting that you pierce it thoroughly; and it is fitting that when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then drain something else without delay; do this many times from time to time, until all the pus issues; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old decrepit men. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the intestines jump out with the issue of the bowel, and by chance the patient dies, and you do not notice. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if you wipe the wound and look to see if the opening of the abscess is small; and if it is a large opening, put strips of linen or fine cotton on it; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you place a strip in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have found in the abscess part of the skin, and you have cut it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen shavings without moisture, and bind it up to the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water quickly and easily, wet a cloth, and put it on the bleeding area many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, then administer treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is during winter time, and the sore or abscess is very sensitive, then you should place cloths and bandages moistened in warm wine and oil; and if it is summer time, and the sore is fleshy, then place cloths moistened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess, wipe it clean, and care for it as needed, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is universally known in the treatment of abscesses; now I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter. 
des soros	of serums 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When boils appear on the head, they are like little pouches of pus, just as the jeweler's pouch for a ring, and there are many similar things. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and some where there is moisture as well as pus; and if there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are such that you prove with all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", of which the form comes hereafter, what it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so let it go through above for a long time. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, scorch without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns when nothing is left; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound and leave it until the next day; and this will carry away what has remained from the night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for healing, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in thick fat, then cut it according to this form, long; and you apply your ointments, and flay it on all sides, and put all your treatment of draining milk for the coat where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess if it is ripe, and for the waist and for curing as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the abscess pierces it and draws out moisture, for they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses have no moisture or pus, and of these was an abscess I opened or lanced in the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if anyone had done anything to it, they would have done just as much harm as cutting into a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chiefly, those which come at the head of children and at the roots of ears, the opening should always be made at the lowest point so that the pus can flow out; and treat it as is appropriate. 
des scrophules	of scrofula 
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come in other parts of the body, and they are very painful, and they are joined together. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its rib, just as the knot and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the likenesses of these scrofula are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some which contain moisture, and some which are malignant and will not obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that case when you see good disposition to touch it, and it appears the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not burned at the nerves of the neck or at the artery or at the conduit, and is not deep; then it is fitting that you cut it off above, and scrape it from each side, and extend the two lips of the wound to one another, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat it bit by bit, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp nor cutting, so that your hand does not slip, and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that staunch blood, and draw out the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased and the wound softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your finger if there remain any small scrofula, and cut them out and clean them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not right that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall by itself, without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then dress it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out all the scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you know how to cut off its root, and draw with force, and sew as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce them where they appear dead; and pierce it as the one before mentioned, depending, then apply tents with ointment and such things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, if the cure of ointment causing flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	from squint 
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have strabismus, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called the "epiglottis" be cauterized; and this should not be done by anyone, because all the veins and the lungs of the patient are affected for those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the windpipe of the throat, it is fitting to lift the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation. 
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we split it below III or IV circles with a small cut across, between the II circles or by the quantity of the cut through the cartilage; and these are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh and the vessels are long and away. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is fitting that he extend the skin of the throat to the whole circumference, then cleave open the chest until it reaches the windpipe; and escape the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the diaphragm, as we have said; and is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe which escapes through the place which is broken, and by the absence of the voice; and leave the wound open for a while. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it all up without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is all torn open and the patient is judged dead, and the defect is in the pharynx. 
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and clean it as long as it was clean; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman take a knife and stick it in her throat, cutting part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found blood coming from it; although it had not pierced a vein nor gone farther than the throat, the veins were ruptured by the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and I cared for it until it was healed; and nothing further happened to the young woman except that her voice became hoarse, and she returned afterward to her normal state; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis one should not be afraid. 
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a pigeon's breast, and it is very common in women; and it exists according to two manners: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fat that we have, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from us from an artery; and there is fear, and it is not right to work with hot irons except in those that are small, and you try and search at all the passageways: if you find it as I said fat, and it cannot go to any vein, cut it as we cut fat, and treat it at all its edges, if there are any; and bind very well, and cure it as it is right, until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of which I will speak of all the resemblances; and now it is fitting that I say all the difference there is between us and being outside. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever lasting, as long as the boiling is not passed, and putrefaction is accomplished; then rests the fever and the heat. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With new growth there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and it begins as a small drop, and becomes large; and they are according to two appearances, either greasy or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a wound, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," according to its shape or chapter which is afterwards. 
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire into abscesses of us is that you take or the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then as it may be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the introducer, and take care lest pus escape. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs quickly, whatever color it may be, let it flow as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, so incise it in a cross shape, and grasp it with pincers, and lightly scrape it from each side, and be careful that where it lies you draw it clean with the new. And if you cannot draw it clean, draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.  
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains there for nothing, the nose returns many times; and if one part of it remains, and it does not bother you, then apply the wound with some corrosive powders, and remove the wound, and put soothing things on a hot abscess, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nose is large, sew the two edges of the wound, and heal it with those who know how to mend flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is beating against you or another, do not hurry and apply powdered vitriol to it, and leave it for two or three days until the wound rots and stops boiling blood; then return to cover what remains in the fresh wound. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Look here at the forms of insertive instruments, and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three of these: large, medium, and small, to encircle fistulous abscesses; and they are also like the needles with which we sew sores, and they are made of citrine brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and are better tried for black lead to encircle the curves of fistulas; and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of needles are of many appearances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and some needles have two curves in three ways also; and some needles have three curves, and are also of three ways; and some needles have two curves, and some needles have only one curve, and are of three ways; and all of this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments with which one cuts are sharp, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, from which one flayed the veins so that one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and of these introducers are the hollow ones made into handles, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them no more than in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and angles, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a flayed fist, according to this form, with which one cauterizes blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back in place so that it heals properly in accordance with the veins and arteries, and never again return to this large shape: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to rot, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to heal them, it is necessary to do so according to this form from this line .b. up to .g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then flay the fat and fill the wound with medicine ointment charring it then assemble the two edges of the wound at suture and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs low and is loosened by its size as it happens to women, then cut it into two ribs above by two resembling clefts so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then flay the skin which is between the two edges and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary in the healing until it is healed; and if it is not healed or the incision is not entirely made because the patient does not want to rest or because of the flow of blood then you must fill the wound with cotton softened in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining part and fat, then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those which contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then dress the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, make it as we said for incisions of scrofula, and if the wound closes inwards, apply a cautery as we said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
