Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut, and the skin above it is sewn together, then many times abscesses come; and just as often it happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; and if you know by which it is, whether for the artery or for the vein, the abscess will be long and perfect.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to avoid the use of iron instruments and those who are at the head should also be avoided, and in the case of a swelling from an artery passing under the skin for a long time; then work the incision as on onicones, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed; then put a needle underneath and let it pierce through to the other side, and remove the artery with a double thread in two lengths, according to what I have taught you in extracting the two arteries that are in the temples; then point the place between the two ties of an intromissor so long as the pus which is there comes out, and let the abscess be released; then administer a cure which produces a scab, until the tie breaks; then cure this with ointment suitable for it, until it heals; and if the abscess is along the length of the vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can from the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place you are holding in your hand, and let it pierce through, and there should be a double thread so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I told you, or a tie from one of the two sides at both ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not come out strong, put another needle all along the thread under the whole abscess to the incision of the first needle, and remove the threads in four lengths; then cut the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut the excess from the heart and leave what is tied; then place a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer cures of tents and ointments until it heals. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in arteries and veins, abscesses come to nerves when they are strained, or through too much work, and similar things. 
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and arms and in all their joints, and it is a sore like abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in several positions without pain; and when it is removed, the patient feels pain, and it is not similar to the body but below the heart; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and that which is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would cause contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, cut the skin with a spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with forceps and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it from a thread and cauterize it, then bone and stitch the wound, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large ulcers hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else a swelling, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and the root is subtle, and the head large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had a small root, and they were cracked open, and moisture ran out. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied them and found that one weighed XVIII ounces and the other VI 3., and the work in incision is such that if you look and see the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of subtle root; then cut at the spatula widely, and have the fire cautery present.  
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if it does not stop, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision with iron, take thread well made, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then release it, and do not cease to bind the thread as long as it holds the artery, and heals through it without effort; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut immediately because of the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize so that it does not grow back; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is of a dark color and poor and milky. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later. 
quant li boude ist fuer	When the arm is strong 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of wound or fissure of the side, and is on the belly and in it are some boils as it happens in other fluxes, or from blood that comes from veins or arteries according to what is ahead, or from windiness; and if it is from the rupture of the side and by the issue of the bowel, then is the color of the abscess resembling the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens from diverse issues. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its hips if it responds, and then returns, and by chance if it is squeezed, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and through great effort. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, without constricting it; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and they are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you see whether its appearance is due to the blood of an artery, or a vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the healing take place. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestines or the bladder, then you should instruct the patient to hold his breath, and be extended straight, then sign with a ring all around the abdomen; then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed all the length; then extend half of the abscess above all the large hook; then tie it around with strong thread or a cord of strong firm silk, and let the ends of the binding be loose; then work half of the abscess extended over the binding, and put your index finger in, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the binding, untie it, and pull out the intestine from the depths of the belly; and if you find the bladder, take hold of it with the hook, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and put in two strong threads, and insert the two needles around what you have done in a cross so that you pierce through; then pull the abscess in four places onto the needles, and if you see fit, remove the needles and leave the place until it ripens, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or cut it when it is thin and rotten, then treat what is appropriate, and close the abscess as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as appropriate, and suture the place. 
dou chancre	a sore 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of chancre, and how one must work by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that the chancre spreads in the flesh, and great caution is needed in its cure, and they said the ancients that when a chancre is in a place where it can be shaved, like a chancre which is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, one must remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, you must not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone ever healed any before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make him bleed if he has manifest repletion; then put the patient in a good place to perform the operation; then shave your instruments or ulcers and the hair from all sides, leaving nothing; and let the blood flow freely and squeeze the area with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding stream is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is dried up; then treat him with another treatment until he is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only erupted; and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicine this resemblance of dropsy which is called “erupted” with medicines, and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the belly and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient is strong of constitution, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should work thus: lay the patient straight on your hands, and have the assistants press the belly at the end by pushing the water to the lowest part under the foot, then take the sharp spatulum according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on two sides. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and in any case it should not be so inserted that it can reach as far as the intestines when you put it in, and you cannot pierce it; then look to see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must make a cut inside at the third rib two fingerbreadths below on the left side of the breastbone; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, the incision should be on the left side of the third rib; and if it is for phlegm, it should be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the cut so that superfluities do not run to the weaker place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, push it in, lift your hand along the entire spatula between the skin and the muscle as if you were flaying, to the extent of a fingernail or so; then pierce the muscle until the spatula reaches the eighth space, and this is the place for the point, then pull hard, and push this instrument out.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a subtle silver cane, and is made of iron or light artichoke, and has a small hole at the bottom; and on one side there are III holes; and II on the other, and I on another; and the head is shaped like a quill pen, and this is the shape of the incision with which scribes cut the quill: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Above the head is the alembics, so that when the instrument comes to the point, you draw now on the instrument; empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than it befits in that hour, by chance he might die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he might fall into palsy, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is held now for the heart that stops the orifice which is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering so, and draw from the point a small quantity; do this every day, and beware of forcing until it remains but a drop of the point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and leave him with much water inside, then use a cure of the burial ground or hot sand, and much sweat or bath and sun, and let him drink; and use a cure of drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	from the removal of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have a hole in their penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its proper place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary as soon as possible, he has not pierced with a very subtle instrument according to this form. 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put a thin cloth of linen over the wound and bind it for three or four days. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose anus is small, if it is treated with a plum stone as we have said, it will enlarge. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the urethra in its place are blemished, for none are born with the urethra at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the marrow, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then extend the head of the penis and the foreskin as thin as a pen's size so that the hole pierces in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, use the remedy of those who stop bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils come in the penis, and they are an ugly sore sight; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a fine needle, cut and cleanse all of them, then put softened cotton on Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafhinicon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the pus is malignant, of a foul color and corrupting, then you must apply cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have caught it, and if the foreskin is entirely over the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the foreskin which is inside first; and when it is sewn, then cure it outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if you are not sure that the head of the penis is pierced, and blackness and corruption comes in the penis or where the scrotum is; then it is necessary to cut away all that is black and corrupted, then bind on a plaster of honey and flour which is made from pomegranate rind and vinegar, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bloodletting is required, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two ways together: that is to say, in the stopping of blood, and in corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is fitting that you put or conduct from the penis a cane of lead, and make the patient piss among it; and when the hairs are burned at the head of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, it is fitting then that you scorch it with a heated instrument, so much that the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if this is a difficult thing to do, it is fitting that you scorch it with a spatula in some spot on the head of the penis and the skin; then separate them well between them, and put a subtle linen cloth softened in cold water so that it does not burn immediately. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a severance of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work willingly, especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the lightest for their health. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greater part of masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions around I dal, with force, and with all one lancet; for it would pierce the heart because there are two layers, and perhaps if one cuts upon those above and remains that below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound must be covered, and the pain is doubled; and in the cleansing which is twice done, the point of the limb is not secure; and in the cleansing of the nail, the iron may accidentally slip out, ruining the work, and often they are born such that they do not need cleansing and I have seen it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Regarding modification which is made to the strength of all the thread I have found the goodness of experience, for the strengths cut precisely both above and below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in a straight line; but let the thread be well twisted around the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the surgical instruments for the dressing is as follows: the two blades must be sharp and cutting, and the blades must also be as large as the handle equally. 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of cauterization is when the heart escapes within the incision; therefore, you must extend it to your fingernail, just as the pus forms an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, take it with forceps, then cut. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days and what is below the penis is swollen, leave it until the abscess boils are appeased, and lightly scrape it; do this as much as you can move, and be careful of the part of the penis, for it will not harm him in any way. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the place of things within a wound with powder, as we have said in our treatise on powders, and if one sears too deeply, and it goes above, it will do no harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	For the retention of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by an obstruction of stone, or of congealed blood, or of the bowel, or of a tumor, or of similar things, which we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone that is stuck at the neck of the bladder, it follows that the patient should be bent on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and he should extend his belly from above his back, and restrain the patient as much as he can so that he does not move; and then the neck of the bladder will be forced to express the stone upward, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it follows that you should administer extraction with all instruments which are called "syringe," of which this is the form: let it be made of fine silver light and thin like the feather of a bird; and let the tube be a palm and a half long, and thin at the tip.  
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of drawing out urine is such that you take a double thread and tie its head to a piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut away the excess wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the buttock; then push the syringe forward until the bladder, and let the patient feel it reach the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless because the one who guides it where it goes is crooked; then pull the thread with all the wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then draw it out, and make the urine flow; and start the syringe again until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved. 
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scaldings or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilled, then make all the instrument which is called a "clepsedre", and this is its form: 
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the end is shaped so that the medicine will pass easily through the urethra without addition, so we can draw out moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see your medicines going into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and pull the string which is inside; if you draw the moisture into the catheter, then firmly push the string back in; then the moisture will enter inside and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of a subtle enema with which we enema the bladder: this is it: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of artichoke, and the head is higher; and below at the breast where the loin joins. Then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture which you see to cleanse the bladder, then bind between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the point of this moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture comes forward, so that the patient feels that this moisture has come into the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, and pierce it round about; then put a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dish, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and bind it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone, and extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between a stone lodged as rains, and all its signs, and which stone one should operate on by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that the sharp point of the stone resembles a sharp point in its subtlety; and it appears like hare's ears, and it scratches the patient's penis, and it can pierce it many times, and then it hardens; and many of these points are founded; and the healing is light for children until they are four years old, and it is very grievous in the elderly, and it is a middle grief for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and push and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the level of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from above; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be below his thighs so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then grasp and touch it inside. If you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut upon the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not chirp at all when touched, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and insert it into its foundation and seek the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, fix it at the neck of the bladder; then press up on your finger and guide it to the place where you see the incision. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the incision will be made; then he inserts the spatulate instrument cutting, which has this shape: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between the buttocks and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and it should be straight on the stone, and your thumbs should be right at the fundament, and the waist should have a cross so that it is wide outside and narrow inside according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance if the thumb which is at the fundament presses hard it will come out easily without work; and know that there are some stones that have angles and margins; if it is grated it is easy to extract; and if there is a part underneath that resembles a button and is round, its extraction is easy. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If the stone has angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it doesn't come out, you should take it out with forceps which are like a file at the head, to pull out the stone so that it does not escape; or put a thin, curved instrument under it; and if you cannot insert it this way, enlarge the opening of the wound, and if the stone is sharp, extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, put in the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then others on top, then treat it forcefully, and the small ones afterward if there are many. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be sewn and a larger wound made. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For the patient two things happen: either he dies, or his urine comes immediately because the veins cannot solder; but nevertheless try to draw it out, or to break it with forceps, as long as you draw it out piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, then apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and remove it, and put a soft cloth soaked in oil and wine on top, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then put the patient back on his pillow, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it arises very well in the place of oil and water, then treat it with diaphycon ointment and basil ointment, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and urine is retained by this, which is known in part manner without straining with the urine: then put your finger in the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and rot it; then lift the wound with sharp and clean instruments, and aid it in all the ways you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour that you treat it, you bind its two thighs together, and apply medicines upon the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is carried along by the penis, and lodged in, and the urine cannot pass; then this is the treatment I mention, that you cut it many times, and there is an excuse for the incision because of this treatment. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already done this myself. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron shaped like this, with three prongs fixed on a fire. 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the trocar into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the trocar in your hand in the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone through to the other side; then urine will come forth soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is quickly broken, and leaps out with the urine, and the patient is relieved; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then put a stick between the two threads near the stone, then pull it out, untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and dress it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It sometimes happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if it ever does, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to uncover herself at her privy parts, especially when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is deeper than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity compels you to do so, then it behooves you to take a midwife well-knowing, and it is difficult to find one, and if you do not find one, then cast a subtle mire; and present her with a wise woman experienced in the lives of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: then it behooves her to push her finger or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it beneath her finger, and recommend that she push her finger in with the sick woman, and grasp and press her left hand upon the bladder formant. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it should be moved gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then press on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it is most movable, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her leg above the stone or below, and make the incision small at first; then put your hand into the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound as much as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with horns. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the resemblances to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood comes, put crushed vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work as long as the stone is hard, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of a stone from men to help you in your work; and if the blood comes, and it is from an artery that has been cut, put the powder on the spot and bind it with tents and bandages, and do not resume this, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient should die by chance; then heal the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, you return to your work, as long as the stone remains. 
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white sac, which is below the heart of the egg yolks, which contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and it is never truly in the membrane of the egg, if we believe that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the egg between the white syfac that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice comes from weakness which comes to the yolks, and is spread out this matter. 
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does it come from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either it is a declining color to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, it is an abscess that has returned, the pus long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very cloth, the abscess will return with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sheath, he feels it well; then when you see to know the color of the moisture, you must try all the inserter, of which the shape is as described before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the introducer, judge what is within. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is fitting that the patient be bled according to our ability and the repletion of his body; then place him on his back, on something a foot high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on his right side, and extend the instrument to one of the two ribs beside the heart; then take the scalpel sharp and cut the skin of the ribs among them along its length until near the nipple; then make your incision all straight in dividing the skin of the ribs until the white flesh is seen, and flay it subtly according to our ability; then pierce the white flesh full of pus with a wide opening, and extract all the pus, and then put your ointments, and extend the white flesh upwards; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the white flesh; cut all or in pieces immediately beside it so that if you do not cut it wisely, the pus will return; and if the lump jumps free from your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the white flesh; then bring together the two lips of the heart of the ribs with a suture, then treat it as the other wounds until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cut the cord at all the suspensions, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if sharp is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound linen moistened in rose oil; and put another linen moistened in wine and oil on top of the two stumps, and put doubled cloths on top, and bind it all up with a ligature according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and make them of shredded wool according to this appearance and let them be sewn together at the neck of the breeches. And one of the legs takes hold above the base up to the back and the other on the side of the hilt; and the other two chiefs on the two angles, and let the whole be assembled in the loop of the breeches. 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And scoop it out in every way that you can until you have removed everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and avoid the flowing of blood, and death from these operations of cutting; and if anything opposes you, whether an abscess or flowing of blood or something else, then treat what opposes you according to what has been said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this procedure because of its horror, then make a perforation as I tell you, and be sure by the signs that we have said that clear water is there; then let the patient sit on a raised seat, then pierce the abscess below the whole pustule wide, and make the perforation as long as the body; and let the hole be large so that all the pus can flow out; then put cotton on the spot and bind it, and leave it for the remaining pus to drain, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the pus to come out at the mouth of the wound, then you must put a pen in it or an instrument with which one treats the pus of hydropsy, of which the shape is given above; and enlarge the hole in the wound, and know that the pus will return, and gather again after six months or thereabouts; and when it gathers as before, then the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the thighs 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there are many dangers, for which it seems to me that it is better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and the resemblances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come on bodies, and even testicles; and it is by much cause. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by superfluity sharp and sour which is spread as boils or of percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is found no pain and it is an abscess grief; and by chance are some abscesses griped grievous and stony, and of ash color, and sometimes comes from new artery or swelling of vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by an artery's rupture, it is known by the hot abscess formation, when you press it with your fingers; and you must not touch it at all. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of vein swelling is known by its disposition to the touch of the fingers, and one can well make a cut on this resemblance, and on the other parts; and it is that you cut out the heart of the onions, then they are raised up high, and the thread goes through the white part, and deliver the suspensory from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already coagulated with these new tools, then you must draw the vein and the cup; and if it is air in the syfac, or in that which is inside the vessels, then you must deliver all that tension, and round the cup. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is behind or further back, it is necessary that you cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks 
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped in a wrapping resembling a blackberry, with the softening of its edges, and the patient groans when he moves; and the cure for this disease is also as dangerous as the one before, but nonetheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspensory below his testicles down to your thighs, on all the vessels which are close to the penis, and hold them with your masters, and extend them; then cut with a sharp scalpel across the place where the vessels are uncovered, and then flay from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples; then he puts a needle where there is a double thread, and ties it at the first place where the vessel has come, and ties it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as the others where we insert the bowel, so that no vessel escapes which nourishes one of the testicles; because by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels come visible, it is necessary to drain the testicles from all the vessels; so that the penis does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries and cannot be helped. 
de la routure dou syfac	Of a broken bone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this condition is by the section that comes to the bone or the stretching on the belly in the part of the bowels, for which the intestines descend from that break to one of the sides; and this break is either of the bone or of the stretching of it, and these two manners come from many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or a fall, or from lifting a heavy thing improperly, and by similar things; and the signs when it is from the stretching of the bone are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal right up to the end, because the bone presses on the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of the sciatic nerve, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and there are diverse abscesses appearing beneath the skin nearby, and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the body's rejection of the sciatic nerve. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never detach the intestines with the entrails, and they are retained within, and cause great pain to suffer to the patient, especially when it is pressed. 
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments for fear, because it is necessary to avoid them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is such that you order the patient to pull the intestines with his hand inside the wound if he can put them back in; then be soothed on his neck between your hands, and lift the thighs; then place the heart above and strip all the skin from the testicles for a long time; then put into the creases of the waist one-inch needles according to what you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the eggs can come out;
