then flay the white membrane which is under the skin of the testicles until the white membrane hard is exposed on all sides; then put your index finger in that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white membrane under the skin of the egg, and between the second membrane; and part that which is behind the egg and between the second membrane; and then push with your right hand into the heart of the testicles, and lift the white membrane high in your left hand and lift the egg to all the membrane towards the waist; and order the attendant to extend the egg upwards, and untie what is behind the ligature; and touch it with your fingers if it has any intestine wrapped around or hard white membrane, and if you find anything like this, put it under the abdomen; then take a needle on which there is a thick thread made of ten threads and put it into the rear part of the membrane which is after the skin of the testicles; after the waist, then cut the ends that appear from the threads as long as there are four threads; then assemble them one upon the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the membrane on which we said that is under the skin of the testicles with a strong ligature of two parts; then wrap the ends of the threads and tie it forming two parts so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter in, so that no abscess may come there; and place the ligature according to the first ligature long two fingers from it, and after these two ligatures leave the membrane which is under the heart of the testicles a finger's breadth wide; and after all the other ones according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the testicles as long as there is no sting, and no swelling as we have said before; then apply wool soaked in oil, and put it on the wounds, and apply the ligature that we said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize white flesh as we have said after incision, for fear of the shedding of blood. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the ligature until it comes out by itself; and if it delays in falling out, so arise a water of hot sharpness, and put upon that which we have said, until it comes out; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch which is together with the vine, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision above lightly below; then cut it in half, and treat the abscess of him who operates, as long as the vessels weep; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the angles, as we have said, and opens the veins; and none of the intestines should be drawn out from the joints, and if any are drawn out, it is bad, and it repairs every hour; and however, if it remains too long in this place, the wound or fistula grows, as long as the intestine is drawn out; and this happens by the extension of the fistula that is in the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swells the veins and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then you cut the place of the rupture swollen wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the fistula that is under the skin that the custom, then take a hot iron and put it on the apparent place of the fistula; and press it hard against the belly, then cauterize the two veins apparent of the fistula on the head of the iron, and cauterize one and the other; then extract the head of the iron, and do not cut the fistula nor extend the thread or anything else, as I have made you know in the cure of the ramication of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if the patient cleans and cares for the wound until it heals. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sinew is constricted and has no appearance in the fracture, and the cauteries are milder in this place, and closer to salvation. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles 
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men because the cartilages that are inside are softened, and it is made to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to heal it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the softened skin above the natural skin; then brings together the two edges at a suture, and if you see fit, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin at three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure as other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread. 
dou chastrement	where cautery 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the patient should be able to answer when asked and know the cure; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauterization is done according to two ways: either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	For those that we do by traction, make the animal sit in hot water, so that its intestines are softened and hang down; then take them with your hand, until they are replaced and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	On castration: it is fitting that you hold the beast and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut on each egg at one cut, when you have well skinned them; and leave no spot where there is a syfac and the subtle syfac which is on the vessels; and this manner of castration is milder than that which is done by traction, because in traction some part of the testicles may remain by chance, by which the beast desires lust; then heal the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways like men: one if between the two testicles it appears as the shape of a woman's nature, or if he has hair, and sometimes urinates standing up. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is for women, and it has a handle like a rod and two prongs. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is such that you cut off all added flesh, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure. 
de la tentigene	From the tentorium 
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tentigine is a wart added on top of the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is fitting that you hold the superfluity of the tenting iron in your hand or at your elbow, and press lightly; and do not press too hard, lest blood should flow, then cure it with another cure until it is healed; and to another sore that is born at the mouth of the wound, apply it, and perhaps it jumps away, and is according to its appearance like a cow, and for this the ancients called it "cow disease." 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed. 
de erratique	Of wandering 
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the parts are small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that has come; or it is by flesh added, or some subtle humor or essence, and it is made perfect in the marrow, or in the sides, or below, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and possibly having flowers; and the knowledge of these is by looking at the belly. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the splinters are close together, appearing on both sides or to the right. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a soft syfac and close to the two leaves, if you hurry, and they are sewn together: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman on her back, spreading her legs; then extend the two leaves as much as possible until the soft syfac is sewn and the stitches are removed; then take wool and moisten it in oil and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie at home each day so that she cannot sew. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syphilis sore is hard and thick, it is fitting that you cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a chariot wheel, suspend it on a sling and bandage; and have medicines that staunch blood, such as aloes, dragon's blood, frankincense, mixed abundantly with egg white; then apply a linen thread wide enough so that the wound cannot close; and keep it long this way, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a boil comes to the flesh, if it should be covered according to this manner, unless it is an ulcerated abscess. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an inflamed abscess which is in the marrow, one must not apply fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which usually occur without a cause, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and we have already said in the division the similarities of others, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve with treatment. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the lul, when they are steeped in marrow, and they do not appear to the feeling, unless it is not cured by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel, are those that one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then remove the afterbirth with tongs, and the cord at its roots, then sprinkle powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gallnuts and similar things, and then take barley flour and mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it extinguishes, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping to the back and breasts without drawing blood; then take flax, soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the area. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and the one that is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a harsh head, so you must cover it as I have said for the thelul; and then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the cheek
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the cheek, such as sore and pierced abscess and herpes and inflammations and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is fitting that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that form a boil; and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.  
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce, but let it rest until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he can lean, and support himself on his back and assemble his feet at the far parts of the leg; and let his thighs be spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good binding; then turn him toward the right side, and bring the instrument used to open the mouth of the abscess.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and you press it gently with your hand, if it is necessary to cover the head, apply a spatula to it; and when the bowels are emptied, it is necessary that you put softened tents in the wound, in rose oil or green oil; and place the tent firmly from the edge of the wound to the margin of the abscess, and put another over the margin of the abscess and over the handle with clean linen softened in water in which quince or apples have been boiled; then treat it afterwards for two days with appropriate ointment until it is healed; and sometimes raise the abscess and the wound by an enema of water and honey, and then of water or long-boiled lily roots and aristoloche; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the marsh, it is fitting that you guard against cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	From childbirth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs that show when you see a woman hasten downwards and desire to smell the air: then the child will soon be born. Then you should know that this birth is according to the natural figure, with the head coming out first, and the secondine following it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press her belly gently so that the child comes out quickly. For when he descends head first, the secondine follows him; and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by a good cleansing. And this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes happens upon its feet, and the body or the head comes loose, and the hands come loose; or it comes upon its belly, or so often, and is converted by chance over its neck, and by other bad figures; it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help her. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes onto her head through natural birth and the woman gives birth hard and the virtue of her is weak, then make her sit on a saddle where the women hold her; and cook oil or fenugreek, and then put the bail between her thighs with the small spatula which has this form: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the second membrane, and cut to its fingernail until the moisture that is within goes out; and take hold of the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must give the woman an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil; then have her drink and sneeze from condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be delivered. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out strong, it is fitting that you reset them gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then overturn the stool onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when overturned; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, cut the hands with the knife that has been placed beforehand, and extract the child, and reset it evenly. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child upon its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, if it is crooked, you must push it upward; and then turn it bit by bit, until it is straight; then take it by the feet and extend it bit by bit. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps as far as the thighs, if commanded to take hold, and makes it sneeze from condition; if the jump is strong, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, if it returns little by little, until it is according to the natural form. 
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take muscilage of hollyhock, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and heat this ointment, then make her sit in lukewarm water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, give her a suppository of myrrh, and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and remove her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child will now jump out. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child upon its knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if it puts its hands little by little; then be swaddled on its neck, and hang its feet down, and be lying off the bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then take its hands onto the belly, and remove the cushions beneath, so that it is exposed downwards; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them upwards, then move the belly up, then push its hands; and lift the child little by little; and order the woman to hold on while the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the issue of a child who comes forth, with one hand pendant 
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to endeavor to bring back the hand; if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie down on the bed and straighten her legs; then administer the muscillage that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, and then try to bring back the hand; and form the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and order her to hold herself until the child is fully born. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the child upon its neck, and let it spread its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back. 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient hold their hand, then turn it little by little, and lift it lightly; and when it is equalized, put on the natural muscilage of hollyhock and oil, as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a stool, and command her to grasp it; and make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the second joints 
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes strong in this manner to all the secondine, then apply the secondine to your finger, until the moisture is drained; and if the infant can breathe on its face and on its neck, then apply the bandage from the elbow, so that it is not held back, and the infant dies; then put the infant inside, as long as you have put it as it should be, and order the woman to take care of herself no more: then draw lightly. 
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens often. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live, if you call them by name; I know they will be multiplied and are delivered from the syfac which devises them, which is tied to the shoulder blade; and at no time do they issue naturally as one under all, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out hard, so the cure as we have said, and be the poultice subtle, and make quickly and lightly what it does; and make thus as it is worth moving to salvation. 
de plusors enfans	of several children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is necessary that the surgeon knows all this, for it may happen; then do according to what is necessary. 
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to work with your hands; then it is fitting that you should know whether the woman is of sound constitution and has no accident or fear of death; then it is fitting that the woman be placed on her back, with her hips inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and let the minister give her a draught of two parts, or bind her to the bed so that she is not treated in the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with broth of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed; then anoint your hands with these oils and mixtures; then insert them gently into the womb; then choose the places where you insert the forceps to be suitable for this; and take care that if the child is attached, it descends upon its head; then place the forceps in its ears or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the groin or near the ribs; and if the descent is on foot, place them on the heel and between the ribs; and it is fitting that you hold the forceps in your right hand, and place the curve between your two fingers of your left hand, and insert them with your whole hand gently, and place the forceps in any of these places that we have mentioned, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the forceps: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place it against the other forceps, or a third if you need them, so that the extraction is even; and then extend them equally by moving from one side to the other, to make it come out, and let the forceps be toothed to hold it, as shown in this form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remain, anoint the bandage with a few drops of oil and insert them into that part, and draw out the other part; and if none remain, put this ointment or higher up and do this until it all comes out. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward in front of the other and it cannot be brought back due to tightness, then you must wrap it on a cloth until it is all covered; then apply a bandage at the joint of the palm or at the wrist, and thus you must do with the other hand, and with both feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of a child is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or if it has a sharp point, you must put the pointed spatula between your fingers, press the head and extract the point; or you can cut it with an instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one. And do the same thing if the child has a large natural head; then draw the bones together with forceps, and if the head comes loose and is extracted by force, split it as long as the moisture which is in it or below it flows out; and if it cannot flow out, cut it into pieces as small as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, pierce it so that the moisture runs out. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and straightening at the mouth of the uterus is easy. 
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is embedded in the belly or breast, it is fitting that you extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture which is there runs; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then thrust your hand in, moistened with marrow, and draw it up to the mouth of the marrow; then thrust in one finger or two, and draw further; and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed by a hot abscess which has come, it is not fitting to work further, but rather administer moist and fatty things; and administer plasters, and make them with soft mollifying and moisturizing agents. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, then apply what we have said about the living child; and if you cannot, then let the arm be broken into pieces, and leave nothing of the second bone. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if he gives it what we have said in abscesses which come on the marsh; and if bleeding occurs, it should be put in tight restraint, and give him other remedies. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had a dead child inside, then she conceived another on top of it, and the other one was born dead too. 
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared on his arm, and it swelled so much that it opened, and then began to discharge profusely. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat him, and I thought for a long time, and could not sew the wound. 
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and one bone came out, and after a few days another. 
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled greatly, for this belly has no bones. 
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought they were bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted the wound, and I drew out the bones with my hands, as long as the woman was in a better state; and I left the woman for a long time like this, and there remained a little bump in the place; and I do not remember this chapter except for the fact that when the masters find a strange thing, they should know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To return the marrow to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here is the form of the pressor with which one presses the books; and at two turns are two heads of two liens. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, let the horns be more subtle than restrictive, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth be of beech wood a finger's breadth wide, and its edge a finger's breadth thick, and a palm and a half long; and midway between the two limbs there shall be two adjustments of the same wood, which shall be fastened on one side and the other, half a palm long or a finger more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the mortise to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood wood, according to the likeness of tongs; and it has two jaws with two adjustments, as you see, a palm long and two fingers wide; and when you see the vulva open for the whole instrument, make the woman sit on her bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then insert the two adjustments together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then operate your hand on the whole instrument, as you did with the tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vulva, so that the midwife does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all mounted, and their resemblances are multiplied; and when the surgeon has prepared them, the quicker the work, and the higher esteem for men by their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not prepare your instruments, their necessity is inexcusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the placenta is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath and then make her sneeze forcefully, while removing your hands from her mouth and nose; and if she expels it this way, all is well. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over the fire; then put one end of a cane or tube into the pot and the other end into the mouth of the marsh, and suck until the vapors come inside the marsh; then make it sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the shoulder jumps quickly. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not strong, order the patient to soak her left hand in sesame oil or marshmallow poultice, and then put it in the position, and seek the second one; and when she finds it, grasp it and extend it slowly and straight so that the marrow does not break during extraction, but gently move it to the right and left, and then pull it out; it will come and loosen. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the ulcer is tight and contracted, we have said the cure is to sneeze, and to fumigate with herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, be careful that you do not go against it; but it is fitting that he who is at the mouth of the ulcer, you tie him to the thigh of a woman, then give him an enema of tetrafarmacon ointment; if it loosens and returns, and comes back strong; but nevertheless, when it loosens there will come foul odor to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is fitting, then appropriate fumigations for this are: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one smokes the woman for the retention of flowers and the afterbirth is this: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it looks like a cane, and we put the thin head in the fire, and the thick parts on top of the coals; let there be smoke over the coals, and heat the lice until they are gone, then start another. 
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the fundament 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather a subtle syfac has stopped it up: therefore, the midwife must pierce that syfac with her needle, and not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and she should keep the lacement so that it does not touch; then put linen soaked in wine and oil on top, and then cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stay in place, put or insert a cane of plum wood, and leave it for seven days, and have it removed when the child wants to go to the chamber pot. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this swelling comes from the closing of a wound or an abscess; then you must cover that closing: if it is healed, as we have said about the cane of lead. 
de la fistule dou fondement	Of the fistula of the fundament 
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the fundament are swellings, and growths that come from beneath the fundament outward, or in the space of two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this swelling is old, it works, and still produces white pus or subtle mucus, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are known by those who experience them through defecation or flatulence when the patient defecates, and perhaps a sudden jump. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder and halfway up the penis; and reach as far as the hip joint and to the knee. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula draining at the base, and not draining; and it is that you put your thumb or index finger on the base, and put a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has tortuosity, insert a tent of fine wool, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and neither pus, wind, nor worm comes forth as we have said: know that it does not pierce through; so hasten to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends to the bladder or to the urethra, then the urine escapes and cannot be held back by medicine. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced as far as the hip joint, then the tendon comes to its place; if there is no crookedness and the location of the pain follows a course around, it is best to leave it alone, and neither medicine nor ointment will be of use; and in these fistulas that persist, there is no cure except labor, and vanity of the foolish remedies that interfere. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not completely dead and not old, there is hope of healing with iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his thighs, and put his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent of linen, or of lead if there is twisting, as far as you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, then you must put your index finger there, and if he then feels that the sinew has been pierced; and whether uncovered or not, where you feel between your finger the sinew or flesh, then know that it is severed; and if it does not work at all, one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We say that one can heal some people well, but this rarely happens; and the help we give is if we heat a delicate cautery according to the width of the fistula as it is said before; and put it all hot in the fistula until it reaches the bottom; and do this two or three times, until you know that these corrupted hairs are burnt, which resemble a bird's feather; and then cure with tents softened in butter, until those hairs rise up, then cure by anointing ointment promoting hair growth and healing. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this, otherwise cannot be healed; and if it enters between, and does not reach the bone which is its foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew between your finger and the fistulous tract, and you see the fistula at that point where the covering ceases to cover the core; then burn from the beginning of the fistula and push forward before the fistulous tract, and then apply the cautery afterwards as far as it reaches the head of the fistulous tract; and the fistulous tract will be delivered and will fall away; then cleanse those damaged pieces of flesh which appear like a bird's feather, and leave none remaining. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood comes, and is cut between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauteries combine two good things: that is to say, the burning of these flesh additions and the stemming of blood and drying of moisture; then the cure of tumors softened in butter or crushed cheese, as long as the veins flow freely, and if the flesh is burned in the wound; then cure the wound with ointments steeped in hard-burned flesh, and they are dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return. 
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the foundation and is distant from the body, stick it with your thumb or finger, and inquire about this. 
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between II is the canvas or linen or char, where it is about to pierce, if there are no other ways of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the III methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure as first; and do not go too far in depth, lest you cut the ligament that holds the foundation, and the egestions come through willingly; then cure it, as we have said; by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it after it has been cut near the foundation, either by tent or by other pointed instrument; then cleanse that faulty flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: if it were a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there are sometimes fistulas according to this manner; and when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is near or touches the base beneath the skin above, then take a probe pierced at its tip in this form:  
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I bend the thread in two, and I put the tent on the whole thread into the fistula as far as the head. 
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is embedded in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread from that hole, so that you pierce your bone or foundation; and grasp the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and pull them apart, and leave it for one or two days; and restrain it several times, as long as the threads catch those cars that are between the two, and squeak; then cure the wound until it is sewn and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, as long as it is not too inflamed. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make for the placement cover so soon, and then the cure, as we have said, until it is healed. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatulia (surgical instrument) with a pointed end from which one makes a fistula is very sharp on one side and dull on the other; for this reason we do not cut what we should not cut as you will see here. 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids 
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: either they are inside the fundament, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they bleed presently, and there is one or several, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still bleed or a drop of sharp yellow liquid or a drop of blood, and have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament is such that you command the patient to strain to go to the chamber, as long as the fundament lets him pass, so that the threads appear; if you hurry, and it cannot be held by forceps, or you hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the forceps cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them off, and powder some hot powders that are in place of cautery on top; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until he is healed; and if the fundament cannot pass, then give the patient a harsh, sharp enema to cleanse what is in the fundament so that it can come out openly; when the patient strains, and the threads are detached from the fundament, the cure is easy; and it is that you take them with your fingernail or forceps, and cut them off, then cure them as we have said, until he is healed, and so that he fears incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you administer the suture according to this manner: take a twisted thread and put it in a needle, then draw the thread above and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and if it is too wide; remove the thread formed, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then place on the foundation a softened cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they weep, and when they have wept, cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of dryness of the veins or foundation 
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there occurs dryness of veins in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no avail. 
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape off the surface with the point of a scalpel or your fingernail, so as not to let it become moist.
dou fremit	Where it trembles 
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small false appearance before the body, and goes very far; and one sometimes finds cold, and feels it too like death's tremor, and comes in all the body, but more in the hands than elsewhere. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane of a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and put that cane on the fremit, until the circles redden the fremit all around; then turn your hand to the whole cane so that you grasp it all around the fremit, and pull it out perfectly, and uproot the fremit from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, make one of a thread of linen or iron according to this form, and let it be thin underneath and wide above: 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, but hold it in pain, and press hard
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one gives an enema of silver or artichoke, or melted lead or malleable iron; and sometimes one uses small and large instruments of these types, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those who are treated in the care of children and who are weak and painful are small. 
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is wide on top, where the belly is tied according to this manner: 
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced within; and it has on one side II holes, and on the other I; and let the belly be where one puts the medicines from a bladder of a beast or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and let there be I space between each hole, then put into these holes I strong thread of raw silk twisted in X or which surrounds it, and assemble the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is within, tie it to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then administer an enema; and that's the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar. Then insert it gently.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it for a disease of flux of the belly, and the medicine hastens to go in, then begin again until it is healed. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base or an abscess, then give the enema as gentle as for a child; and this is the form of a gentle enema on which the skin is extracted: 
des plaies	of wounds 
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and of medicine according to accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or the wounds where they are made, and of what they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are made by the blow of a stone, and the cut of a sword and knife, or a lance or a musket or an arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to their location on the body, such as a wound that strikes on the neck, or on the head, or the breast, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the head, for the memory will come in its chapter. 
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if you are careful whether it is from the blow of a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: then make it heal quickly from the cephalic vein itself if little blood comes from the wound, and let the healing be on the contrary side of the injured part; and forbid the patient to eat wine and heavy meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal, let his flesh be reduced and he should not drink wine nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if a boil comes, cotton softened in rose oil alone or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot boil, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder which I will say a bit later here; and if he has moved it, then put on some ointments until it heals. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by stitching, then bring them together with sutures as I will say for abdominal wounds, from stitching. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered from the bone and can be gripped and held only by a point, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats such as heads and boiled wheat, also fowl and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten flesh, and it does not reach the bone, cut off all the rot, and clean it thoroughly, then treat it; and if it has an artery in the wound or vein from which blood flows freely and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: and it is that you put this powder on it which welds as if fire had melted it.
