Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder subtly, and apply it to the wound, and extract the form, until it burns well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do this with chalk alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has dried the wound. 
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has cauterized the wound, do not put this powder on it at all; but put on some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it is running; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterwards. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck 
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves in the neck or the artery is cut. 
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment alone and not apply anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation with the brain, which is the highest member, is.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed. 
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of pus, then pierce it lower; and if the artery is cut and blood flows, then untie it, ligature it, and cauterize it; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is preserved through which the flesh goes, then stitch the heart onto the cane of the throat, but do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape; and then extract it gently, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then scrape it; and if there are pieces of bone, then pull them out all together if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound rots, and is cleansed and aligned. And if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder that I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter. 
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of spear or knife 
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife and the wound is deep, look to see if there is wind coming from the wound while the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal it then with tents and other remedies, as long as it heals; and if it cannot heal, and the work is done, then know that there is a fistula; if the cure is done as it should be. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the front, back, or side; its treatment depends on who is in charge. If it is large, it should be sutured; and if it is small, with powder. And if it penetrates to the bone, and has fractured pieces, then you should clean the wound and treat the broken bones if they are loose; and if they are not loose, leave the wound to fester, which will make extraction easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, judgement should be used as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	regarding rupture of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small; from a great wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, which prevents entry; and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because the intestines are put back in more easily if they are not put back in one by one; for the intestine swells quickly as soon as it feels cold so that it enters less easily; and therefore a medium wound is preferable because one can move the intestine to its place better than the others. And know that a rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly, and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other proper stitches are common with other wounds; and all the same they are more suitable with the stitch of the belly, and I will say one each and declare it. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines is protruding, and it is easy to put back in place, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you cook in lukewarm water squinant and cypress and spikenard, and remove the intestine as long as the swelling is gone; and never make this wine astringent, and it is milder than one that just draws out. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you remove the intestines of sharp or high and bad things are cooked, because through this is aligned the entrance for little; and if it cannot enter, then make a cut in the wound with the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is milder than the size, that none should cut without great necessity nor should there be; and here are the instruments for cutting: so cut within the curve and do not go beyond, and see this form: 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, if you can put them back into their natural form in their proper place, do so, for this is worth much. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, it befits that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture from the belly is in one of the two parts, put your mind to it so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it befits to administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put what has been prepared for you, and hold in your hands the instrument which has a whole suture in its hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common way of suturing, and it is that you take one needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the beginning of the wound two spaces, and put a needle where it has a good strong thread; and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two sides of the subcutaneous tissue, which is under the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce that part, and assemble the two edges of the subcutaneous tissue together; then strain a double thread around the needle in two parts, then assemble the two sides of the wound evenly, and then leave two spaces, and put another needle; then tie the thread like you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need needles, as long as the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and large, because subtle needles cut through all the flesh, and too large ones cannot enter well: for this reason they should be medium-sized; and do not put the needles too far away from the flesh and skin so that they don't cut and open the wound before it heals; then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths over the ends of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this way of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because you can use one needle or two. The second suture is common, and it is that you assemble the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the subcutaneous tissue together with one needle where it has a medium-strong thread; and when you have pierced all these sides together, pull the needle to the part where you started, in the way that one sews drapes; and put space between each suture the thickness of a small finger; this suture heals the man, and I sewed a wound on a man's belly or stomach, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a handspan large, and it affected the intestines well two handspans in size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back his intestines after they had been outside for XXIV hours, and the wound was sutured up to XV days, and I treated it, and he was healed. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And those who saw him thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I put nothing more on the wound than old cotton twice a day, and washed it with water and honey until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced the flesh straight through straight, leave the head of the thread or twine or where you have passed the needle, and make it pierce through the other side from the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the furriers do furs, and that you leave one time the thread on one side and take it up on the other, until the stitch is completely finished. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is as some do, who bring together the two parts naturally, and apply one of the heads to the other head, in this way: insert a needle or the head of the thread nearby, and pierce only that place, and leave the two heads of the thread; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part to that within, with the two heads of the thread; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to that within, in two other heads of the thread which are on the other side; and this is the easiest manner of stitching and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and none testify against it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it; and one must put one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than the others for bellies. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of the other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it, then replace the intestine, and the cost; then put on powder enjanrant char, and if the fire has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound swells; and sew the thread, and let the sifac and mirach be soldered; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to swell, old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in several positions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may cause commonality with the principal members, it is fitting that you moisten a linen cloth lightly in tempered oil or rose oil, and put it around the groins and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or decay in the bowels, which often happens, then give enemas of warm red wine, and likewise if the decay comes as far as the intestines; and pierce them within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.  
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the plantations of veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the worm comes out of the wound, put it back in place as you would the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, you must bind the part which is black so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut away what is between the binding, and hang the two ends down from the underside of the wound until further out in order to make the extraction easier when the worm's head comes out, and the wound swells. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the fracture of the bone 
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is pierced and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and the excretion and flatulence came from it; I treated him according to what I could, and did not cease to refine until he was healed, and his wounds closed. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sutured, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his stomach; and he did not have any pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take thread with large heads, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips so that it tightens its mouth above; then cut the head off, and this will stay so that it cannot loosen, then put another thread afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is all closed; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If these worms burn in the intestine and cause no harm to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this intestinal thread which is well stripped, then tie it to the end of a fine linen thread twisted together. Then thread it through a needle, and sew the intestine, drawing it together at the break; and this method of suturing is nothing but according to the way of faith and hope. If the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the intestinal coils, there is no remedy nor safety except subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be 
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows old, is called universally "fistula," and the same when it is healed and drawn inward. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its nature a hard and white knot, where there is no pain, and it is also raised like the feather of a bird; and sometimes it has a clear channel, and other times it is thick; sometimes it is small, and other times large; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only because of one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or flesh; or because of its wickedness; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, that does not allow flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or because the leus is rotten and the matter is of bad quality; or because the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a pestilence; or because the nature of the region is slow to digest, and slow to heal, and swollen by nature; or because there are veins or bones. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary for me to teach you the treatment of a fistula which is made by handwork. 
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if it happens that it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the place I have said, and you have confidence in the cure and you see it, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight, so you can pierce it; and if the fistula is twisted, then search for it with a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends easily around the tortuousness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot properly search for them with tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings, because the moisture will pass from one opening to another and purify it; then pierce it with bloodletting according to your ability so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and remove it perfectly, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you and remove the corrupted matter and the decayed flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in a straight place, then it is necessary that you cut perfectly as much as you can, then put softened tents in medicine boiled in water, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments that promote healthy flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said; and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not hinder you, nor the principal members as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove all the corruption until it is completely gone. Then cure with healing agents as long as it is healed. And if it is not healed and returns to its former state, know that you have not reached the bottom: uncover and scrape until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too advanced, and you cannot proceed; there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature. If there is only one small bone corrupted, and you can grasp it with forceps, extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose. If there are many bones, treat them all, leaving none behind. And if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cauterize the moisture and flesh, and free the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something promoting decay on the wound and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, then you will remove the bones more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as those of the leg or thigh, spread the corruption only so that all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part that is corrupted and reaches the marrow of the bone, you must sew and cover it all up to the corruption, then treat it until it is healed. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much so that the humors went to the leg and it swelled into a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the healers, through their folly, worked so much on it that they opened the abscess, and they drew out a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many openings which all discharged pus and moisture from the body; and many healers treated him for about two years, and he had no one skilled in the art of healing, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was flowing out through the openings into a large container; and the young man's body became red, and he had a yellowish complexion. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pushed a tent into one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all sides of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption was coming up to the bone within; I scraped away what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with hot medicines for a long time, and could not solder it; and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and scraped it away, and then removed it, and strove to solder the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm of the bone, and treated it thoroughly with all its marrow, then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and soldered quickly, and it was not necessary to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation it often bled, but it was healed completely, and in place of the bone there grew a hard flesh, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contrariety at all, neither in coming nor in going. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be treated in this manner: take a linen thread and tie it to the head of the bone that appears, and command someone to extend it upward; and put another linen thread thicker than the first thread, and tie it above the flesh that is below the bone, and stretch the head so that you draw the corrupt flesh underneath, and expose the flesh on the place where you see that it must be treated, so that the silk does not stain the flesh; and put a coal or a wooden plank below the bone to burn away the corrupt flesh; and it must be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and treat it again. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or a part, then uncover all the flesh. Then put a coal underneath, and then burn from one part to the other the corruption, and let the burning be as long as the corruption; as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint and burn the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the corruption is at the point of the hand or foot, it is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire about this corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not oppose you. And know that there are many instruments for cutting these bones, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, their thickness and subtlety, their size and smallness, and their hardness. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each semblance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of illnesses. So consider the instrument which you need as it suits.  
dou feu	Of fire 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder may rot either from within or from without; and when you have medicine that will corrode it through the application of medicines, and it does not profit, then it is necessary to cut off that limb up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or from the greater malice of the loss of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and rots after the blackness, since the corruption goes from member to member, and takes hold of the whole body; if you hurry in cutting off, and if it is from the sting of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and the like, if the corruption is in the head of the limb, then cut it off, and do not give it space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, so that the cut is at the joint, so that the gangrene does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, so that the cut is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the amount of its virtue; and do the same when the gangrene comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it rises into the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one of the bandages downwards, and another upwards, and you cut away the flesh which is between the two bandages at a span wide, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and put on each side a linen cloth so that the sewing does not touch the healthy place, and it will cause the patient other injury and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you are working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, and then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his right foot: there came to him a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on the back of his right foot, spreading until it covered the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut off his foot, and was healed; and long afterward the corrosion returned to the back of his hand, and he came to me, and I put things that repel on him after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corrosion; and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I tell you this story only so that others may do the same, if they need to. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in fleshy place, and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; and then it bursts and breaks open, and the pus leaps out, and the place remains empty, just like a vessel; and the skin which is above is also delicate as a fine cloth, and does not run down to the bone, nor down to the nerve, and such a sickness is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin which is such that you cut all around this skin, even when it is delicate as a cloth; and it does not swell because of its corruption.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are certain that the flesh will burn and the corruption is not complete, and the flesh is tough like leather, then treat it with an enema as follows: see if the breast is large and the bowel that comes out has a foul odor, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: take aloes, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need and mix it with water and honey, and give the enema through the breast and remove the obstruction; leave the medicine in for two hours, then extract it by squeezing; repeat this many times until the breast is cleansed and the pus is removed. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, do not allow char to form there; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest place where it is, for when the bowel is in perfect condition, do not allow char to form there, and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in such a way: that the bowel runs easily downward, and do not leave any of the bowel; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and spread them on a linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut at strong points around the opening of the breast so the hole is larger than the first, then spread ointment often on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the opening of the wound to align the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and that which is outside the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the bowel, and know what runs from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough, digested or undigested; and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not; and when your medicine has been spread in such a way and you see the nature that leaps on the opening of the wound, know that the breasts are already healing, and approaching health; then untie it in the morning, or on the third day; and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast swells with undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not aerate. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons linger for a long time, do not despair of health, for healing approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly, and others who heal quickly; and if a lump of undigested food remains in the stomach after many days, know that the breasts do not open; and if the breasts are slow to open and are hard, apply drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointment diafinit, for it contains a great deal of vitriol, and is the last medicine. Take ointment diafinit and make it with rose oil, and rosewater from old wine equal in quantity; then melt it and use it; and this same makes thicker fat when ointment diafinit is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey when it is taken off the fire; and then spread it on a cloth and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer an aristolochia longa root, and roots of lily of the valley, which are also like flour of beans and centoire; and use them as simples or composites: grind them and make powder, and put them on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is perfect and makes an impression in the bone, or hard members, or limbs; if the cure of a fistula, as we said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the finger 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A felon is an abscess that forms under the nail of the finger or toe, or sometimes it appears in other places; and when it becomes envious, and no care is taken, then it comes to a boil, and runs and spills pus as long as it runs to the root of the nail, and sometimes it runs all the way; and corruption comes even to the bone, so that there is a foul-smelling pain, and the flesh of the limb becomes wide, and its color is dark.  
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the superfluity that remains from the ulcer, then cauterize the wound afterwards. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to grow in, and the wound, it is necessary that you put a piece of rag under the nail so that it does not touch the flesh, and lift it up, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it away and treat further, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone corrupting, cut it away as we have previously described, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is hard, swollen, and the patient feels great pain, first you must heal it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, cutting across above it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, apply something that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the deafness of the hand 
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two growths that are born in the hands of some men are all fleshy, and sometimes there is bone where there is flesh, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of these are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in some of us of the fingers. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any place of the body does not move, and he who is born at a joint of the body, by chance moves; the size of the one that is fleshy so is light, in such a way: taille it at its root with a broad spatulum.  
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grief to heal: if you hold him tight. 
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born or about to be born soon, it is fitting that you first shave the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for him, then treat it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Solderings which come together at the two ends come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things. 
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you mend this suture so that the bone may repair according to its natural form; then place between two tents or cloths softened in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of very thin lead, as long as the bone is joined, as it should be. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a soldering comes to any of his limbs with the palm, then cover that solder as it should be done. 
des vils	of old 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large vessels wrapped full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many parts of the body; and they occur more in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry loads than others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purging with colocynth to him, and then apply balm of basilica. 
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is according to two manners: one is that you cut, and draw forth the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein, and treat it all thoroughly. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The setting is according to this manner: first raise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick sinews are softened, then pull the leg from the patient above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then draw and drain black blood with your hand from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtue of the patient can suffer; and then bind it up and instruct him to abstain from meats containing coal-black color; and begin again the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and help the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the bone is according to this manner: hold the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it over fire, and then cut the place at the vein along the length of the knee, or in the part below to the ankle; then scrape the skin with an awl, and flay the vein on every side, until it appears when one touches it; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then put the ray underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then draw it to the awl lightly, then cut in another place above III fingers; then scrape the skin on the vein until it appears, then lift it with the ray, as you have done, and draw it to another awl, as you did first; then cut another incision, or several if you need them, then lift it, and put it at the joint of the foot, then pull and lift until the second incision; then extract it from incision to incision, until it is all free, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and lift it, put a needle through all the strong thread doubled, tie it and pull it, and put it under the ray, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out; and make sure that it does not cut, for if it cuts, one cannot pull or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient; and when you have drawn it all, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and care for it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the sinew is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cleave it diagonally, but do not cut it completely; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cuts the vein if it is curved and does not cut unless it cuts the vein; and it is of a large curve because if it were subtle it would cut the vein but let it be as thick as we have said, and this is the form: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is injected into the legs, in warm parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth which has no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the rot that comes from under the skin, just as serpents and worms come inside the body, inject between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude, just like a root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder joint is open, it is fitting that you wrap around a piece of linen from three and a half to ten fingers long, tie it off, and leave the linen hanging on the leg. And whenever it swells at the fire, wrap it again around the linen and tie it off; and if it is too long, cut off part of it and wrap the rest, but do not cut it at its root, as long as it all comes out. For if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and decay or pus, and a bad sickness; for this reason it is fitting that it be treated bit by bit until the head, and nothing remains there or of flesh; and sometimes this vein when it is treated is five palms long, or ten. And one man came to me, to whom it issued from ten palms long. When you cut it, it spurts out one finger or hole, and pierce it through to the bottom so that everything comes out; and let the matter which is inside be emptied, and apply at the place medicinal substances to prevent decay any day, then cure it as the abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never with this vein only hands, and likewise when it opens in the joint of the foot or leg, and there comes much pus and it spits out blood; treat it as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land “beef disease,” because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and one feels it well from limb to limb, as long as it is under the skin where it goes, and jumps strong; and it arises from putrefaction of certain humors, just as come worms and serpents and lampreys and ascarides or belly-worms; and doubt is had of its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cleansed and drained, if it cannot be removed when it goes: then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong tight ligature, then cut upon it and drain it thoroughly; and if the worm is completely embedded in the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and can move from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and soon after, I saw it rise as a worm on her shoulder, faster than anything else, like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another; the pain departed from that place and struck into her shoulder, and then soon after ran through all her body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it would now turn around her body, just as I saw it. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.
