Nevertheless, I had seen many who had wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I had not wanted to do so, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and therefore the constrained windiness appeared; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are fleshy, and who have moist bodies and covered veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, tie above and below hastily; then cauterize on top until this windiness constrained at the place is forced out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, let the cure of those who drive away windiness be done, such as fetid pills, and pills of serapis, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge. 
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kind is such that some have large points, and small ones, and hairy ones, and soldered ones; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and those which bite in any member bite according to two manners: either in the principal members they bite, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the head thus lies in any place of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you here afterwards, appear to you: it is fitting that you refrain from extracting this arrow, for death comes afterward in many dispositions; and when these evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow enters and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is upon the brain, is darkness and stupor and vertigo and redness in it, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge without odor from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there comes moisture from the wound white looking like pus, and leaping also as burned charcoal; and if these signs appear to you, hold yourself back from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh hour when it falls upon the heart is that it is near the left breast and also feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the seventh hour moves just as the pulse does, and there comes forth black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death approaches. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has not been removed is that without any discharge of pus it leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and desires cold air. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow lodges in the covering of the buttock, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great sighing, and all the limbs of the shoulders move. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance, some undigested meat may come out of the wound. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the belly or bowels, and no part of it sticks out through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure, nor for extracting the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow sticks in the bladder, and the urine leaps and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine of the back and the forearm and the thigh and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me so that you may do likewise. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell or entered into the root of his nose: I tried it, and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he drew out an arrow that had fallen into the fat under the eyelid below, and the arrow was barbed, and could only reach the point towards the fire, and it was a large arrow like a Turkish bow, all of light iron without ears; the player was healed, and no bad accidents befell him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears; I shaved the beard, and I handled it so subtly that I removed it, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew an arrow from a man who had it stuck in his belly, and thought he would die; and then after he had passed thirty days, it did not change its position; I cut above the arrow, and I hooked it, and drew it out, and he had no bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man to whom an arrow has fallen or stuck, and the wound was sutured on top; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural position, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sutured; and he remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I extracted an arrow from the house of the princes of the king, which had fallen in the middle of his nose, and there was a small decline on the right side; and the arrow was all covered.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I have all but one subtle attempt at it, and I do not feel it; and he feels pricking and pain under his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for three days and sewed up the wound thoroughly, and kept the patient a long time, until he felt the arrow in his bones one day; and he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put corrosive medicine on the wound for several days until it opened, and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow rising in its place; then I added more of that corrosive medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared clearly visible to me; and after four months the edges healed well, and then I enlarged the wound so much that I could put tweezers in it, and move it from one side to the other, but it wouldn't come out; then I did not stop refining and devising different instruments until one day I got some good tweezers, according to their shape which will be shown at the end of this chapter, with which I extracted the arrow, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	And I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows so that you put your treatment on what I do not say because the books cannot contain everything; but wise masters find many great things and on what is present and lacking, they find nine works, and nine instruments for removing foreign objects that occur in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit the limbs where they are lodged except according to two methods: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and the one that goes out by the place where it enters is an arrow embedded in its flesh, and it rarely comes out now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it is rotten, and the opening is enlarged; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, pierce around it with a very thin instrument, until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then remove it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it is equal after a few days, for if the arrow comes as far as the syfac, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed further than in the bone alone, and does not reach as far as the synovial cavity, and the patient remains for some days without any ill accident, then you may draw it out. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot come out by force, then administer poultices around it as I have told you; then heal the area until it is healthy. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, then if you can feel the whole shaft; and if you feel it, then draw it out with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then widen the wound until it is large; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, then remove the flesh that is stuck to it from two sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you draw it out more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it be until the sinews around it are ripe, then treat it, for extraction will bring relief. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting a nerve and a vein, and place something so that you can move the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do this, then place him according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it appears nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place so that one can see or feel it apparently: cut then upon it, as much as the pincers may be able to take hold, and then extract it; if a jump occurs now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out forcefully; and if there is a part of the arrow in it, push it all the way through; and if it were bone, and you see that it needs to be pushed hard, do so with the instrument having its tip pointed, so that the point of the arrow enters the hollow of the instrument. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is fitting that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is appropriate. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the flesh or the chest or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close, and you can grasp it, grasp it; and beware of grasping the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs with which one treats arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape: 
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the end of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as this is its shape: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps for pushing and for knowing if it is this: 
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one can bleed, of which there are XVI on the head; to wit: two beaters which are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the two arteries which are in the two temples appearing; and two veins which are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein which is between the forehead; and the vein which is on the head at the birth; and the two gullets which are at the neck; and the two veins which are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins which are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are three in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and common people call it “vein of the head”; and the middle one is called “fascia”, and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and common people call it “vein of the heart”; and the basilic is on the right side, and common people call it “vein of the belly”, and it is on the arm, and it is the one from which we bleed, which appears manifestly on the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvation vein is the one that is between the little finger and ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg or foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the pocket on the left side, and the second saphenous vein is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The vein of the head that are after the ears helps against old catarrhs and migraines.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for ancient migraines, habitual ophthalmia, and a body filled with watery tears; and the quality of this bloodletting is as follows: 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting from the cephalic for old facial illnesses, and for migraine, and for redness.
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the amount you see; then untie the patient's collar and tie the vein tightly until it is healthy and never do this work with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not fitting that the flame be too strong; and the healthy side, for the bone is close by, and the flame may break if it is subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with these things, and the tigne, and the redness, and the swelling in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their bloodletting is that the patient twists their neck with some kind of cord, as before; then they let blood, and it may be a short cut or a long cut, or a small hole. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then make a running sore as much as you need and then bind it with cotton and bind it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The sinew of the vein where it joins is good for the ague, and for strong fevers, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old. 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sinew of the two tendons helps with the constriction of the bladder, and at the beginning of menses, and with many illnesses, and with impetigo, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and estiomenes; 
de la sainie des leivres	From the sanctity of books 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The vein of the lips above helps with coal in the mouth and corruption of gums and fissures of the lips and pain and swelling. 
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is to make the patient sit in front of you, and pull out their neck as I said; then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and because there are small black veins around them. So take both of them. And if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then take the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, for it is the same way. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein below the tongue helps after the vein in the head, and it is for the constriction of the throat and eye diseases and mouth diseases; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and lifts his tongue, and looks under each side a black vein: bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, because below are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins through which we commonly bleed are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a wide, sharp flame-shaped knife, or with a subtle olive-wood instrument as sharp as cutting knives, and called "anesil"; and they are large or subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see. 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are full of thick blood that is visible, and that contain thick and cloudy blood; and this is the form of olive oil. 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more delicately pointed, and it is for cauterizing delicate veins, where there is subtle yellow blood. 
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly; and it is fitting for the healer to bleed it moderately, and to wash away from the artery which is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he severs the artery, and blood flows, then it must be cauterized as I have said; and it should not be pierced by the flame, but cut like a chisel. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilisk does not open manifestly, it is necessary that you extract it and change another; or if you want any vein of it, or you make in its place the vein beneath the arm: it opens manifestly; and apply the cup to the flame as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see that you know the location of the vein, it is fitting then that you remove the arm, and touch the place until you recognize the pulse; then mark the place with chalk, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein where the flame does not burn; and be careful not to wound the artery when you see the swollen place for this is an artery: wipe it off.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upwards just like the urine of a child, and the vein is red and thin, know that it is a vein of the artery: hurry then and put your finger on lengthways, and remove your finger if the vein stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move it for the patient; be careful and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it comes, and you have no medicine, then bind the artery when it appears, for the head of the vein retracts; and stop the blood. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of fig and cut it, and take one half and tie it well until the next day. If the bleeding stops, it is good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and the stopping of the bleeding is not bad in several positions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the bandage on the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle helps it to draw blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is fitting for the healer that he washes for the nerve which is underneath, and if he points too much with the instrument, and finds the nerve, it swells and the healing is grieved, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in any man because of its subtlety, then it is fitting that you heal it with an anesthetic instrument; and avoid the nerve as best you can. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make the incision long. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic helps, for it draws blood from the head and helps with them; and it is necessary to bleed by pricking it with olive oil flame or myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and do not worry if one must try the first time, and start again; and by chance the muscles swell in some people when one tries the first time, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is not administered except to preserve health and avoid future diseases; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins which are: cephalic, fascial, and basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of spring, summer, and autumn after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and it should be done on the first day or the third day after two hours or three. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to the sick has no determined hour, but when need is of day or night, in all hours and at all times; and it does not behoove to bleed children until XIV years, nor a woman carrying fruit before the fourth month until the seventh.  
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Those who have passed sixty years should not bleed themselves. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way it may be, it is fitting that he cleanses his bowels with a mild clyster if he has retained much phlegm so that the veins do not carry harmful superfluities to the principal members; and no one should be bled who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk so that he is forced, nor those who are dropsical; and one should refrain from bleeding after colic passions, vomiting, discharge of the bowels, multiplicity of intercourse with a woman, labor, watching, and fasting, and those in whom all virtue has been weakened, or by something from an arm or the body.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as quickly as cords in a lute, and if some are full of windiness, so that when one puts fire on them, they withdraw from the flame and cannot open the vein, then one is of these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason it is necessary that the bloodletters be advised in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein works the first time, it is good; if not, start again a little lower than that place or higher quickly, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the arm is swollen, and the patient fears it, leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: lest boils might come; nor enter a bath, then resume the lancing if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or the blood thin subtly, and you doubt that as much blood will not issue as you see, pierce in that same opening straight to the very bottom of the vein; and perform the work hastily, so that the arm be swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the incision again, and put a poultice of oil on it, for it draws the blood from the body, and is milder in this place than the oil; and thus administer the oil poultice in every vein that you open, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing does triacle and boiled rue, when it is put on the place; if subtle the blood spreads when it is too thick. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not yet drained except at the time of the small opening of the vein, then hurry and put a moistened sponge in hot vinegar and salt on the place for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has come out from the vein, and if it remains there after several days without blackness or greenness, do not harm it; and if you see, put something made of aloe or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, mustard, or similar things. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there occurs an abscess and swelling in the vein of the basilica; put then your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft under pressure from your hand, that appearance is bad.  
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything we have said, for fear of cutting into an artery; but put a dry plaster on it to harden the area, and then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for one who is strong and robust, and needs bloodletting, that a wider incision be made, and the lancet be broad; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed frequently in small amounts, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by puncturing; and this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive blood flow and severance of nerves, and is worth more than a long or wide incision. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body is weak at the time of bleeding, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, let him eat softened bread before the bleeding in thick syrup, or syrup of aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chiches, and well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the outflow of much blood, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and fragrant subtle syrup and uses other things as we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to heal his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the quantity of his continuing strength. 
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bandage their arm after the first bleeding, and they have strong flesh, then they should bandage seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another injury, it must heal on the second or third day. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood in the body which is already heated, and it brings fever; so it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and to widen the opening so that it flows freely; then when you have restored all the conditions of health, place your hand on his pulse while he heals, so that death does not come instead of healing, and this happens often when the healer is negligent; and it is not right when you see the arm loosened, and make the blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor if it is crooked, let him extend his arm quickly for that would be bad; but leave it until it heals the second time; or apply a point of flame there, so long as the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein flows freely, and place a piece of linen sharpened into a point upon it and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then do so in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein at the elbow is cut instead of the vein at the temple because it is thicker. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is such that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the flesh is red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein appears well, and then the blood is let now across, not lengthwise nor breadthwise; and the opening should be wide, and the bloodletting done very close to the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, then put the hand back in hot water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is worth for all liver diseases, and this is the way: draw the hand out, and plunge it into hot water, until the vein swells if you see it; and if the vein goes sideways, and if you cut through it in every way, it does not matter anything; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are underneath all naked of flesh; then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and wax on the vein to heal quickly, and do the same for each vein. 
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew of the left hand is worth against the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you to the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The vein of the saphenous is worth more than all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of phlegm, and disease of the kidneys, and thighs and old legs, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its remedy is such that the patient plunges his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it swells, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and a great many veins run above the foot; therefore heal it either with a wider vein, or at the ankle, which is better. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cauterize it on the foot, be careful of the nerves beneath and cauterize across as in cutting; and let the flame be numb. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water and let the vein drain well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sinews fail the first time, begin again the second time above a bit, for the flesh is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make the bandage of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle bone, and its pain is worth the pain of the hip when it is for hot blood. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of her vein is such that the patient enters or bathes, and twists four times on the ankle above, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, draw the vein in all the ways you can, and crosswise; and it is worth more to cut it, for the flesh is thin, and she is very full of blood. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, look for a vein that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and draw as much blood as you see, then untie the ligature, and put cotton on top and remove it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping glasses 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made from horns, or gourds, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventosation which is without striking is according to two manners: either it is with all fire, or without fire; and ventosation which is done by striking and by extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is all above the head; and the others are below the neck; and two others on the two sides of the neck; and the cupping glass under the chin; and the cupping glass on the two shoulders; and the cupping glass on the buttocks; and the cupping glasses below the two arms; and the cupping glasses on the two legs; and the cupping glasses on the two ankles; and ventosation does not draw blood, except for small veins which are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it weakens no one at all, as one does with bleeding from a vein; and it is not fitting that it be administered, neither with all fire nor without fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness to cup, or for custom, let us administer them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and at any time; for there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and some who find repletion and redness in their face, and their head, and neck, and darkness upon them; and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swelling of the tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who faint, and see by night blood and dread and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is less than a month old, we order him to be cupped after three hours of the day. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sinew of the thigh helps to relieve the headache...that comes from them, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in place of the sinew of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those who are of cold complexion or have diarrhea, for it does them great harm; and therefore it should not be used by the elderly nor those with cold diseases of the head.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover often become stiff, and therefore it is necessary to put the cupping glass a little lower because of the risk of stiffness. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Bloodletting is done on the neck in place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this it is good for narrowing of the bladder, and a fissure in the channel of the rectum, and for all other ailments; and it must not be pressed too hard, for if it holds too firmly, it causes blockage or illness in the stomach and heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the two ribs at the neck is as effective for head pains and ophthalmia and migraine and strangulation and toothache, and is done on the site of the basilic vein; and you must instruct the patient to press their hand down while it's being applied so that they don't sever an artery and blood doesn't flow. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping below the chin is good for diseases of the mouth, and for gum disease, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is placed where the saints are on the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and swelling. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Bloodletting from the temples is worth as much as bleeding from three veins in the arm because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to apply too much heat, for the flesh there is thin of flesh, and below are nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is on the croup is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for illnesses below, and it behooves that the cupping glass be large, and be of iron, so that it has need to draw well; and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break, and it would make great wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the cupping glasses on the legs bleed freely, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the reins, and the bladder, and loosen tumors; and they are placed on the two calves, and the two ankles, but nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring emaciation in many conditions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply a cupping glass is such that you first put it empty and suck it up temporarily, and quickly place it on the skin, moving it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the place red and swollen and appear the redness of blood; then remove it and replace the cups, and take care in the disposition of bodies, because there are some who have thick flesh and clear pores: it is fitting to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and one deep hole; and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it is fitting to strike twice; the first time to make the path of the thick blood thinner. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out blood little by little, we only strike once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we begin often; and if the blood is thick, we pierce it deeply, and its ends should be so that the heart is pierced frequently, and it is fitting for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have many pores, that you moisten the places of the cupping glasses with oil aperitif and dissolvent: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or almond oil sweet, or oil from the seed of the gourd; and if it is in winter, with oil of cress, or lily, or chamomile, or other similar ones. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or balm, or oil of anise, and the like. 
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person whom one heals has tender flesh and large pores, it is not fitting to put any oil on them, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or water of blackthorn, or water of pumpkin, or water of porcelain, or other similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, should rise with rosemary, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things. 
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities should rise from old wine, or vinegar water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not suitable to apply a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping, and he must wash himself when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the one who is healing is choleric, and if his wound is too hot and inflamed; it should be that he takes cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and eats little, and roasted meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is half old and half new, and eat little, and eat sparrows and pigeons and young birds; and on the day when he will be purging himself, he should drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men sometimes ginger or musk before or after the purge, to strengthen the principal limbs; and let the wine be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are placed without cutting are those that are placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and gout, and on the belly and buttocks and loins and hip, because these members do not suffer to be cut, and we only do it to draw blood from one member to another, as when we put them on the breasts when the child bleeds; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as when we put cupping glasses on the belly and buttocks to reduce the member; and it removes pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, and by its attractive virtue it removes the obstruction by chance, or dislodges the stone from its place; and so it does when one puts it on the liver and thigh when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in this way we fill the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is thus: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two palms wide and half a palm long, and have at its side in the middle a small hole, as for putting in a needle, and let it be of iron, sharp in front so that it does not prick the patient when placed on the limb; and it has in the middle a crossbar of iron or wood, to put a wick in, and they are large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who use them; for the cupping glasses for children are different from those for the elderly, and for thin people than for fat. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this cupping glass on the limb: take the wick of wax or linen, and put it within the cupping glass through the stem which is within the cupping glass, such that the clarity is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and your two hands should be upon the perforations as we have said, such that when you wish to see if the vapor goes, remove the cupping glass; and take the linen as before, and begin again often if you need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered for illness of pleurisy, to all sharp pains, it has neither a stem nor a hole and is not administered unless it is full of water, and is placed upon the limb only; and this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suppositories are only administered in limbs where one cannot apply cupping glasses due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in those devoid of flesh, such as the breast or nose, and other similar ones; and the quality of the user is that when you find suppositories that are in sharp, sweet, clean water without impurity, take them; and put them in a sharp, sweet water for one night, until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies; and then let it be bled from vein and cupping glass, then rub the limb as long as it is red, and apply the suppositories; and when they are full and shrink, if it is a place where one can apply a cupping glass, apply it for it is worth much afterward. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.
