If not, if you lift the place of a nail, and then sharp, very well, and then you breathe on it; and if the nails grow too soon after the body's flesh, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on top until the flesh is numbed; and if the nails are multiplied, put powdered vitriol or galena, and similar things, on top until they are numbed; or you put half of peeled beans on the place, and leave them until they burn at the place, now it will stop; and if you need more, take other nails. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the warts do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or you put a needle in it until the wart comes out, and then put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they fall off, sprinkle powder on a poppy head and salt crushed together, or ashes, they will fall off now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the things which are treated in this chapter have never been seen by anyone nor read in any of the ancient books and letters; and for this reason the knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found any good one; and I do not know anything except through the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have so much studied that I have treated the science there, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have shortened it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are administered, as I have done in these two previous chapters. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting then that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and stays upon virtue, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hasten to heal the sick person on one side and the other, if nothing hinders him, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his temperament is very hot, or too cold; and forbid cold meats, that is to say cold dishes, and meat of birds and goats, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, nor of spreading of matter in the limb; if the sick person returns to his former government which he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is fitting that one nourish the patient with foods that promote fattening, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and peas, and veal feet, and cow's udder, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at half breaking it can return to its place more quickly than a fracture. 
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be properly set or rejoined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset the broken bone with large splints which bind and join the limb together, until it is strengthened as it was before; and do not move it from its place, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish it with plenty of meat, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to splintering, and others to sharpening, just as the point of a pen for writing. 
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with just a small crack. 
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each manner, it has its own engine and its own proper instrument in restoration according to what memory comes to its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted and appears clearly by touch and sounds under pressure from the hand; and when there is no twisting nor sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it may well have twisting or fissure or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting that you move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come hereafter, and then now subtly extract it. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes in splints, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary now to put them together equally, just as abscesses come alive; and if the abscesses come hot, leave them for a day so long as the abscesses are appeased; then put it equal to the muscle that you can lightly and wisely, and know that its restoration is easier than its restoration where there are pieces; then extract it, as it suits afterward. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into two pieces, whether it is the hand or foot, or at the top of the hand if it is a small limb, or into two cords, or one cord and at the top of the hand; and set the limb according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken limb are loosened, you will reset them all together in their places as much as you can, and be careful that by your work no injury nor pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it straightens beautifully, and do not force it too much, do not press as those who bring on by their work a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, chastise the patient well so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other manner; and be careful that the limb is secured so that he feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except perhaps a little, and it is necessary to put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and see that it is set straight, so that crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in size, shape, and severity. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and hands and similar ones: it is fitting to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is fitting to wrap them with a wide and strong band, for the wide bands embrace the whole large limb and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no flaw.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing for the abscess that heats and removes the swelling, and leave it like this for several days; then strain on your splints, and let them be half the width of a cane, or from wood used to make wedges, or palm reeds, and let them be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint which one puts on the fracture be a bit thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as is fitting for the limb, whether small or large; then remove the splints just as you did at the first time, and then bind a thread evenly over them, as in the first time over the fracture; tighter below, looser above; and it is necessary that the threads are moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and are of soft flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in works by fools who make their bandages with twisted linen thread, it is a great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not right that there be less than two finger widths of space between each splint. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore from the heads of the bones after tightening them in their joints, put under them cloths of flax, or wool scraps, so that they do not bleed. 
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the heart is broken, I will say its cure hereafter. 
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to set all broken limbs on the first day. 
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to put splints on them before five or seven days, or more according to your judgment of the hot abscess that follows; and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this confection, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster that restores the fracture in many positions, and also for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fractures and dislocations and torsion: take three bay leaves and ladani and enule and asafetida and gum arabic and mugwort, each X; myrrh and aloes, each V; alechil IX; and make powder, and mix them with yolk of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly and is worth to many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is good for torsion: take mugwort and vismalve, each X gr; myrrh and aloes, each IX gr; agaric VI gr; Armenian bole X gr, and grind well, and boil with vinegar or the white of an egg, and administer it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and bones dislocated from their places, and soothes the pain arising, and uses the size of the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and soak it in lye and cooked oil, and put it on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removes pain. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to soften the remnant of an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marsh mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is inflamed, mix it with coriander water moist, or of water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another kind of plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of marsh mallow, and flax seed, bugloss, sweet melilot, and wood sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all an equal part; and grind, and boil with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb for restoration except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one must put on the broken limb, to restore things dry a hot poultice, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another kind of plaster that is good for wounds and pain: take mugwort and horsehairs cut off, or bird feathers, and vismalve, and mix them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little afterward, and be careful if the patient feels any pain, or if the bone has not moved from its place; then do not loosen it for several days.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess grows and reddens and has pain and swelling is gone entirely, and you need plaster and bandage, if it starts again as you did first equally. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, do not untie it except after III days or IIII or V or VII; and never leave it for XX days, according to what you see, as long as the fracture heals and approaches the adjustment of the flesh above; then restrain more than before, and thicken its flesh as I said before; and if you see the place dry more than necessary, know that swelling cannot come; therefore, apply a bandage of warm water every time you untie it, and this be every third day, and leave a poke at the wound; by this work therefore, you cut off the swelling in the limb, and quickly amend what the foolish doers, who twist the limb: it is bad, and these are dangerous works, and I see nothing else but to leave and work straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of fracture 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone up to the syfac which is below the bone, as the hawk or hatchet does; and because of this, this manner of fracture is called "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or a crack, or chips of stone, or a chair on stone, or other similar things. 
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating close to the membrane which is under the bone, or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small. 
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is healed into the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and makes the piece of bone go in, and the ends are smooth like those that blacksmiths make when they strike on anvils; if the stone enters inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have soft bones, such as the skulls of children; and it occurs in all these types of fractures where small pieces are detached, such as splinters; and I will speak of them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by traction on them, and inquiry with probes, and by the corrupted flesh which is upon them. 
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The likeness of hair is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs strongly upon it, if the fracture appears black. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the patient's conditions, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, spasms, pallor, fever with chills, and the eyes coming out and reddening, and other similar things in various states, then it cannot heal without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeless situation, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment. 
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nettle rash first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the time that you can. 
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone is corrupted, and accidents come as we have said. 
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes as far as the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the divided part thus: and take hold of the head of the patient firmly, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more often than you can, and if discharge of blood comes to reveal the bone, or an abscess forms, help it with what is necessary, and fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil; and make the wound rest as long as the abscess that has formed subsides, and be assured of the discharge of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method if you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another incision larger than the first one. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of different sizes of instruments, some three-sided and others wide, and they are pointed, and are made of tempered iron; and work lightly so that you do not dull the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer cuts with trephines, not so much that they do not pierce beyond the bone where you are testing, and it should have a margin or circle on its point so as not to let the point go beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the type of bone, so that you have trephines for all of them; and this is the form of the three kinds of trephines: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put the drill on the bone, and turn at your will until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the drill elsewhere a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with the knife the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pincers; and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, it is fitting that you leave the splint which remained from the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisor; and if any of the small bones remain or no scales, then remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galicians say, which is more secure; and the praise very strong, and this is their word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lentiform incision tool, which has this form: 
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting tool is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet above it, so that you gently tap the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth underneath; if it is close to the bone, lightly scrape the bone, for one can scrape it well without harm, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the cloth, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then you must grind behind that roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle razor which you must have in various quantities, so as to administer the most suitable one in each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave before with great razors, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not cease to do this until it is good. 
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In all the other types of cutting and subtle breaks, it is fitting that you administer treatment according to its direction; and this is something that is not answered to one who has put his study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the fistula is uncovered, it behooves you to take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it upon the wound; then take another cloth doubled into two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it upon the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not burden the fistula, then apply a bandage over it, and do not bind it too tight, only so that it holds the wound; and leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscesses that are there are appeased, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily root, wheat flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put it upon the wound, and now administer cleansing medicines without biting, and take care that the wound is now clean, that you do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to collect, for when pus gathers upon the cloth covering the brain, it will corrupt and fester, and cause great harm to the patient; for when one puts something biting upon the fistula, it will act through it. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt. 
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackening does not come except for the medicine that has been put on it, which has such power, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and in glue I cloth, and put it on the syphilis; then cure it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose are broken, or only one, for they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless you force it to bend or twist, and then it heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you put your little finger or the hole of a needle and place the broken part inside your index finger, and in the pouch by deflating, so that the nose returns according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot come back into place, then you must put it equal to the head of a nail, a large prick. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, redo it in the same way, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscesses have calmed down, then apply at the head of the wound cloths of linen. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you press one side, it is broken on the other; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that one must soften the bandages with butter and change them every day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in a preparation of egg yolk and mill powder; then leave the bandage on until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes put goose feathers in place of bandages, and if it is wrapped around the wound, hold it steady, and blow on the patient among; now do what you see. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come up while you are working on them, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a drop of diammonium. 
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess comes, apply a plaster made with flour of fennel and powdered frankincense, mixed with egg white, then place on light bandages and do not bind it tight; and if the fracture in the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments for this purpose, then sew up the wound, and treat it with things promoting healing flesh and soldering, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound within the bone, treat it with splints, and place canes of plum, until it heals. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only superficial, and not broken in two, but pushed inward, so a connoisseur can slightly recognize it. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, put your index finger of the right hand and gently push the fracture inside, and hold it with the other hand by force, and set it equal.  
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, so that it is equal. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move, or there is a break, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put cerate on the broken jawbone, and put a double cloth on it; and put a large star well made on the cloth, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it up with strings as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the appearance changes, untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and put a plaster on top, made of mill powder with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the cerate; and put a light linen cloth on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, do as we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone is removed; if so subtle, remove it with suitable instruments. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need. 
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, if the wound is wide, and put on it bandages suitable for that, to promote flesh, until it is healed. 
de la forcele	Of the forceps 
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forcele breaks several times before the shoulder, and the fracture is according to III manners: either it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the broken bone is; and the other extends the neck toward the part; then put the fracture equal to your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor swelling. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it thick according to your necessity; stretch and loosen the bandage, and remove the sphere with your hand so that you put the fracture in equal alignment as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder back out because it has come in perfectly, then it is fitting that the patient lies often on his backside, and puts under the shoulder a medium pillow, and have the assistants push the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised. 
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then straighten the fracture according to your judgment, and if you find it shattered, it is necessary that you cut into it; and treat the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any pressure, take it to one of the incisors that you have; but put the forceps under this instrument, to guard the suture: 
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not hollowed out, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and it has two heads, as you see, and one is broad, and the other narrow, as is the break in the wound that you have made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, if the wound burns, and the break is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, if apply the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, soak a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on. 
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incisions, is that you put on the bone the plaster of powder from the mill and egg yolk, and put light bandages on top, and put a splint below the armpit, if you need it; then take a very large bandage of a handbreadth wide, and put a double drape over the bandages and the plaster; then take a thin stick three finger-widths wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage up onto the collarbone and below the healthy armpit and below the injured armpit; and bind from each side, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move on the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the ligatures loosen, then tighten them; and have the patient lie on his back, and put under his armpit a small pillow when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder up high; this will lighten the fracture from the force by raising the shoulder, or you tie his arm to his neck and do not untie it unless evil accidents occur, until 20 days; then renew the plaster if you see that he needs it and remove it and leave it like that until it is restored; and it is restored at most in 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the breaking of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates widely and it cannot be moved except by touch; if you set it according to the shape of the break and reset it according to its natural form in all the ways that you can, then put on top powdered mill with plenty of egg white, light bandages, and a double linen cloth. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out before, and not below the heart, then lift it up, and bind it with splints, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe a hot abscess. 
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot 
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in two, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the beginning. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken below, it declines downward, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and everything else, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the hair in the broken bones, and they see it well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with his hands, and subtly makes them equal in all the ways that he can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then puts plaster and bandages over the fractured bone, using a subtle powder of salt or some other light substance, and wraps it in a cloth, and ties it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turns the bandage around the back, and tightens it evenly, and examines each hour the binding, and if it softens, he loosens it; and if it is necessary to untie it because of corrosion or itching which comes to the place, or pain or an abscess, he hastens and unties it, and removes the plaster, and treats what has come there in a manner of cures; then he applies the plaster again, and keeps it on until it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs comes only from their thickness after the back, and chiefly inwards, and they do not break except because they are slippery; and one can well feel it by inquiry as to whether they are. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break straight as it should be. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a plaster, and remove it with a spatula, if you need to. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is leaning inwards, then the patient feels great pain and sharp stabbing, as well as pleurisy, because the bone points at the lung; and he suffers from shortness of breath and vomits a lot of blood, and this is very dangerous, and the ancients treated it with great difficulty. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, in order to drive out the fracture. 
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, so that hot abscesses may not come, if they have not already come. 
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if there has come, so he is healthy. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one puts cupping glasses on the place to suck out the humors, and this seems reasonable enough; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass might attract the superfluities to the place because of its weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say one should cover the place with linen moistened in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to keep the bandage even, then it is cured by the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine. 
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone which points at the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument below to protect the syfac; and then one must trench the bone, and pull lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and cure it with plasters until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if boils come, put them on cloths softened in rose oil, and put them on the place; and treat it while the place of those that it befits to a boil, and let it lie often on the side where it should be, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and it also happens when it rains; and so too in the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take care if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in several positions, and if he moves them and feels well when they are extracted and do not move, know that the junction of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if there is health or not, see if his feet are softened, and if the accidents are in his hands, and on his back there is windiness and expulsion without volition; and when he is turned over onto his stomach, there is expulsion without volition. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and he wants to get up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if he does not work on his cure. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this mishap does not befall him, the thing is easier. 
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you warm it if there is a hot abscess; then put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is calmed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage; and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels the pain, until he is healed. 
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover it with the heart; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then cure it with ointment containing charcoal, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your left hand in your pocket, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then apply plaster and a bandage on top, if you need them; then remove it, and if there are any broken bones, do so, and remove them, and cure the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip 
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes it happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, it would not be a small matter; and for a long time it declines towards the bottom, and causes the patient pain in the area, and swelling where the break is. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it as long as you are above the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is in the head alone, then put it equal to that fracture, as long as it is in its natural shape. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inwards, then make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that break appears to you. 
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back in place, apply a plaster, then put a splint of wood or horn on top, and immobilize the fracture so that it does not move; and apply pressure below the ribs, as long as the ligament is even. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it until the abscess is appeased, and put on what we have said before; then return to restoration, and extract it as it should be, if there are no bad accidents; and this is the way. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder 
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, so you must restore it according to one of two ways: the first of which is that you take a stick plain of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two limbs with two ties, and lift them up high, and place the patient on a chair; then he places his broken arm on a plank, so that it reaches the armpit, and has given it a bend in the plank, then he leans on some heavy object where the ministers extend it downward; then he puts the hands together at the fracture site.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one sets the patient on their back, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two ministers that one hold what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below at all the ligature, and each extends at his part. 
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to their part. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is fitting that you place one bandage halfway below the armpit, and the other toward the elbow, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is toward the elbow, it is fitting to put the bandage lightly, without effort, as long as the fracture is aligned on the arm and on the elbow; then align the break, as it should be, and remove it, if no abscess comes. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes, do not extract it until the seventh day, and put moist linen soaked in rose oil on it, until the abscess is calmed; then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you place a plaster on the break, then bring the arm up on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put the cloth, and extract on the shoulder, and on the arm so that the arm is in its place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints and place a wider and stronger splint on top of the fracture, and have two finger widths of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture by three finger widths on each side; then strain on the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter on top of the fracture, harder and less in distancing. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the bones and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it to be bandaged until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the bandage every three days, so that itching does not swell nor come to the place, or the nourrissement cannot come to the member because it is too tight. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not loosen the bandage for three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of equally thick wool, and look every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, nor are the bandages loosened; if it heals by the power of medicine, and give him the meat which we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is at first delicate; and when he begins to recover, let it be coarse. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be bound together for forty days altogether; and then you should untie them and administer baths and ointments for healing the place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and obstructed, it will remain for one day or two months. 
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm 
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "humerus," of which one is small, and it is that which goes into the pouch; and the other is large, and it is that which is below, towards the little finger; by chance the large humerus breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when large ones are broken, so is the healing bad, and more grievous than when they are broken all together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it is necessary to gently extend it, and set it straight. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is a large muscle, it is necessary to restrain more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher up, so that the patient does not suffer any hardship; then extend the minister's arm below his hand or at the ligament, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any that is detached so that it holds onto the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before, on bone and sinew. 
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a singular chapter; so take care. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses arise, then make a cerate plaster from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the plaster subtly on top until the abscesses are quieted.
