Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax, and he puts a plaster of flour from the mill with plenty of egg, then he puts on the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be now stronger, and a little larger than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in several positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and pull more above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the fracture be soft and damp, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is drawn be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And watch over the limb and the joint after a few days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is fitting that you bathe the limb in hot water, until the itching is soothed; and let the limb not be tightly bound at rest. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone loosened, and similar things, if so address. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are careful so that the nourishment cannot reach the limb, because it is too narrow, then you must soften it a little and leave it like that for several days, until the nourishment comes, and then remove it. 
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things which we have said happen to the patient, do not loosen it for up to 20 days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	When one is injured, then they may put their hands on their neck, and make sure their necks are aligned, and avoid movement and shaking, and sleep on their back; and know that this fracture is healed in XXX days or XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the constitutions and complexions of the humors. 
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and like us we have two fingers which have a bit of splintering, and there is nothing else but weeping many times. 
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is fitting that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit straight in front of him evenly; then put his hand on the outstretched table, and stretch out the ministers the broken bones, and put them equal to the mire, as long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in a linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the middle of the foot, make a sphere of linen cloths and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot; and then bind it with a long bandage, and let the star be as large as the palm of the hand and bind it as it should be. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is below, it is fitting that you place a splint above and another below on the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand and bind the ligature between the two. 
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our fingers, if it is a thumb, then set it straight as it should be; and remove it with the palm, and if you see that you put a small straight stick to lift the fracture, and it does not move; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index finger or one of the others, then set it straight, and tie it with the healthy finger which follows; or tie them all together in a shape that holds, or put it on a stick, like a pouch; and take care in the restoration and placement of a hot abscess, and help those who come to it, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see this well when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration consists of tying one ligature above the fracture and another below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his linen to his equal share; and this is when the fracture is between the bones. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, one of the bandages should be towards the hip, and the other bandages below the fracture. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then let the bandage be below the knee, and let the extension be downward; then put the hands on the bone equal to his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural form, and then put the plaster, and the bandage, so that no abscess comes. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and your treatment; the incision is made in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with a bandage doubled two or three times, and leave the excess, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and bring the end of the thread above; then turn the bandage on the leg and thigh, then put splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then place eight pieces of cloth softly between the leg and thigh to make the constriction equal, then begin to tie three or four twists on the fracture; and when you go further up from the fracture, loosen it less; then take the two ends of the thread that you have put between the thigh and leg, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you reach the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as is, until no abscess or swelling or other likeness comes.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, so that it loosens and straightens what came out of place, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that stick, then they should be removed if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the area and draw forcefully; and treat it as we have said, until it heals. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the thigh broken in this way as one puts splints on it, just like in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in the restoration thus made does not ring the patient. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions. 
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee hollow 
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that on the street of the knee there is often no fracture, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is but a crack or a hole, and occurs in every wound, and in every wound, and this is well known. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done when one puts together what is broken to its right place, as much as it can be moved, then apply a plaster, and put a round splint on it if you need to, and hold it as it should be, then observe all the provisions that we have said in other fractures, such as abscess cautery and other similar ones; and apply to each accident what suits it until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of a leg fracture 
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other is called "foscile"; and all kinds of fractures occur in it as they do in the arm, and therefore the restoration is just like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg is twisted in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bones are broken, turn them forward. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it turns below. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and make it equal, and tie the splints equally; but nevertheless, if there is a bad fracture, and there are several pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and according to your ability. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two strips of wood that are long enough to cover the leg from one side to the other and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them around with two bandages above and below, and tie them in the middle so that the leg cannot lean either to the right or left, and thus it is well done. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones of the foot 
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	There is no fracture at the ankle, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and there are two possibilities, and there are no other conditions except in several positions. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a bone in the foot that is broken, and you see these bones rise upon each other, so set the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on his where the bones are raised, then press it so hard that they return to their place; then put plaster and bandages on top, and put a small table under the belly of the foot with two inches high, then straighten the foot carefully, and after you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things that you need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated. 
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, so restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and make it a bit wider, then put underneath the foot that table that I have said, and strain it gently; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, so put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and strain the table underneath the foot; and let it be standing on the head of the table below the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as soon as we have said; and help each accident as it is necessary. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone by the dagger 
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of a woman's nature are broken, make her sit enlarged, then incline her to the part of her back, and let her be held from behind; then fill the woman's nature with cotton, as large as I can stand; then lift the woman, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton will jump, as it comes to the entrance of her nature, and the bone will return with the stick; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of a lamb, and tie a cane to the hole, and push the whole bladder into her nature; then blow into the cane until the bladder is inflated inside: her nature will return the broken bones; then let it be filled with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone from which a man's or woman's shoulder is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the thigh; and these nearby fractures are not hidden to him who applies his study and experience, and understands my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For a fracture, he signifies to us in several ways the right path for restoration: understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for 3 days or so, and it will be healed quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be cleansed now, so that the cleansings which we have said testify to it. 
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, and you have no other remedy, then start again to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, so that abscesses do not form. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes there, leave the restoration until a new day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you will cause bad accidents. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the chest uncovered, it is fitting that you set it straight lightly with your hands, with little extension. 
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear suitable for putting it equal to your hands, then the surgeon has this instrument which is of iron, which has VII or VIII in length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary that he engraves III or IV, according to what he needs in each cure of fracture; and let it be round and a large point, so that it does not bend at compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," because it is fitting that the curved head be placed on the top of the bone that shows; and once the end is brought back so that it returns to its proper place and is equal with the other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have power. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot put the bone back, as we have said, then use the point of a suitable instrument for this, either an incision knife or a saw, according to your ability; then cut away what remains in the bone, with sharpness and small shavings. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you set it in its place, then moisten the bandage in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is summer; and do not put any cerate or other thing on the wound where there is oil, lest it cause rot and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and bind a covering all around according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many foolish surgeons have done this, and have caused death or corrosion on the patient; and let the tightening be gentler and softer than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents might come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not right to put splints on it; but wrap around it, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the gut in the wound begins to move, remove what you have put on it with all wine, and apply healing ointment, such as Tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound. 
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be aligned in such a way that the bone runs down slightly. 
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it passes and it cannot be soldered but continually bows back, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must want the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause this pain. 
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or some other manner of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it according to what he says in his chapter before this one. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thighbone or shoulder bone, and other similar large bones, do not draw it out, for many times death comes from this, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come from solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a bad thing to see the shape of the limb; and by chance it cannot make the limbs do their natural work. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the swelling is fresh: if you administer astringent medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg white or with oil; and put them on the swelling in compresses, and bind it well, and do not untie it for several days; and then unbind it, and begin another, as long as the swelling is removed; or you bind it on a piece of lead well made; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut it off with a knife, removing the superfluity that appears; or have it shaved by someone, until it is removed, and heal it until it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains afterward with weak and delicate limbs, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not come to the limb; or because of a multitude of risings; or because of too great movements, not at the proper time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften the body, so that his blood is multiplied in him; and you administer a bath, and give him joy and leisure; then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts great inflammation, and bathe it often with warm water, until the inflammation corrects the limb; and it returns to its natural form. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a crooked limb after health 
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish ones have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and great evils come from it, and by chance death; nevertheless, if the nodules and the torture are fresh, it behoves them to be softened with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as diachylon well made, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with the fat of gelded pig or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or you take fat figs, and crush them with bran of wheat, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.  
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut up to the bone, with a subtle incisor lightly; and put attention and study in the care. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations 
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury. 
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it must now be brought back without delay. 
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limb swells, and by chance if it is reset with pain in its place; therefore it is not good to move it while it is swollen: many times it causes spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, make a poultice for the patient, then leave it until the abscesses are healed; then bathe the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as they come into their place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws 
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It sometimes happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are separated from their places a little, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the bottom, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through several manipulations. 
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a way that the ministers hold the head of the patient, and put their eyes into the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be free, to put it back evenly; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let him look at the same spot until it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if the two jawbones are together, then apply rose water and oil until they soften slightly; do not force the resetting, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening it, put soft cloths on it made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with many bandages; and let the patient sleep on their back, and let their arms be between two cushions so that they do not move them either to the right or left, nor make any effort to chew but take light food as long as the pain is gone and the jaws are healed; and then eat what they want lightly, and do not bother to open their mouth to eat and drink as long as the jaw is well healed and sound. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not converted to their places, fever and accustomed colds will come, and possibly loosening of the belly, and possibly vomiting of pure bile. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times they die in nine days. 
de la forcelle	of the fork 
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The cautery cannot dislocate from within the continuation of the leg and foot, and it is dislocated sometimes by force, and one feels it well. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms; then press the place formed with your palm, and it will return; then put on the plaster and bandage it, and remove it; and the head which is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates any time, reset it in its place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus likewise is returned the head of the shoulder blade when it is removed from its place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates towards the armpit below; and the second is towards the side of the buttock; and by chance it dislocates upwards, and this happens rarely; and it never dislocates behind for the shoulder, nor inwards for the nerves; and often it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially for those who have little flesh, because for them it is quickly dislocated; for those who have enough flesh, it is difficult to dislocate, and it returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens that some men experience a bruise or fracture, and their shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of it. 
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must test it until you are certain; then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocation is known when it is pulled down towards the shoulder, and notice the difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find manifest diversity between them;
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the attendant raises the patient's hand upward, then puts his thumbs under the armpit, and lifts the joint forcefully upward to its place; and the attendant raises the hand, and extends it upward, then puts it downward; it will come quickly. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in three days afterward, it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water; and be given a mollifying and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of altoe and fenugreek and melilot in water, and be applied; then let the patient be laid on his back, and put under the armpit a wad of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then let him place his heel on the wad, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister hold the head of the patient so that he does not move down; this shoulder will return immediately now, and if you see that the resetting is according to this manner: and it is fitting that you have present a man who is larger than the patient; and be straight towards the side, and put his shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pull the hand of the patient down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is also done in another way: and that is one puts a long burning stick into the ground, whose head should be as round as a pistol, and neither too thick nor too thin; then it is put under the patient, but let him have cloths enough above, and the patient stands upon the length of the wood; then his hand is stretched down on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things we have said, then do this cure: take a stick of two arms in length and four fingers wide, which has a round head for easy entry under the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie on the top of the beam with cloths underneath so that the patient is not injured, then put it below the armpit of the patient; and extend his arm onto the top of the beam for a long time, and tie the shoulder on the top of the beam, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on the rung of a ladder that is wide, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging down on the other side: the joint will come back into place now. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, you must put a sphere of equal wool under the shoulder, then apply plaster mixed with powdered mill flour, incense and egg yolk, over the entire shoulder and around it. Then tighten it under the shoulder carefully and turn the bandage on top of the plaster, embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus. 
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is fitting that he should rest a little, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then rest more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or some other cause, you must administer cauteries at three points, as described in the chapter on cauteries. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint was never fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation which is towards the shoulder, and the breasts, or behind, is made by impulse, and extension of the hands, and it administers another place; and heals as long as it is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and slow movement, then let the patient bathe many times, until the stiffness is relieved and it returns to its original nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	Of dislocation, what is done. 
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the knife is dislocated at points, and at points it returns; and if it is dislocated on all sides, both in front and behind, the dislocation is not set back because one can see it and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick knife with the healthy one, if you can see it openly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is lifted, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is fitting that you soften it in such a way that abscesses may come, for if abscesses were to come, it would be harmful to reset it; and perhaps it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is at the back; this is worse than the other dislocations and causes greater pain, and perhaps death may occur. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it can be brought back like this, that you extend their hand with your two hands; and let their arms be spread out, and the hands in front according to the curve of the elbow, up and down, and push the joint at its knuckles together, or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is forward, it returns when he doubles his hand onto his hand, and touches the root of the palm or the costal which is dislocated. 
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and when the minister extends the arm, and holds it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when he looks at the joint, apply oil to the joint with his hand, so that it softens the joint, then push the joint firmly, until it returns to its place; and when it is in its place, put dry plaster with egg yolk on it, and hold it firmly, and bend the arm at the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then begin again with the plaster and bandage, and leave it like that for several days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put on the joint a fatty sheep's wool, then leave it for one day and one night, then bone set, and let him enter into a bath; and when he sweats, if he rubs the joint temperately, then puts the wool on, and then enters into a bath; and thus do it two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see that, put cow dung moist heated with butter, and strain it on; it will return to its position. 
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is light, more than the other joints. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and make it equal, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it as far as it returns all the way. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the doctor put his hand on that part of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good; but if not, apply soothing plasters to the abscess, and leave it thus without restarting. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain crooked; do not harm the patient further than necessary as long as his hand is weakened and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut or the artery; there is no other remedy than to extract it with a cautery nearby, and perhaps nothing else will work. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind it and leave it like that. 
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some pain, then apply hot water, and rub it until it is healed. 
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulders of the hand 
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the shoulder joint dislocates in any direction, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then it is dislocated and pushed into your pockets until it returns. Then support the head of the shoulder and bend it towards the side where it is separated; leave it for two days and then set it straight that same day; bind it at night as we have said, and unbind it during the day, make it move, and bind it again at night; do this often until it is tight. Do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand and do as you did before, until it is healed. And do the same when it is dislocated in another part. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Concerning the dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back  
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the limbs jump involuntarily, and he cannot hold them, and often some member is softened, either both thighs or both arms or one.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or from shocks or similar things, the ancient ways of treatment were said in great detail, where there is not much profit in all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in different ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gibbosity that comes to the breast beforehand, there is neither medicine nor cure; and also that which comes straight on both sides, and it cannot be cured except for that which comes properly to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in an equal place, and have a strain beneath him so that he does not bleech; then put one ember at the head in the ground shaped, and the other at the feet, and tie a linen thread below the patient's buttocks, and the other at the haunches, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and let two ministers hold the threads, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two embers; and let them be well fastened, the ember as we have said, and the minister put his palms on the spine shaped, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board three arm's lengths long, and place it under the armpit, and have the patient lie on their side, and put the head of the board under the armpit, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the patient put their feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not work, then do it with a wrench which turns in the hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you place two charcoal pieces at the head of the patient's arm, and two others towards the feet, and have between each charcoal piece, above and below, a hand's breadth in length; and have in each charcoal piece one hole, through which the cord runs, and let the charcoal pieces be firmly embedded in the ground so that they do not move; and between each two charcoal pieces place another charcoal piece turning, from which the cord turns, and have on the two turnings two small charcoal pieces a hand's breadth long, to turn the cord; and then tie the cord which is among the axles to the turning piece towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet to the other turning piece, and let each of the assistants turn his turning piece all along the cord, and the master places the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are even, put a desiccant plaster on it with plenty of egg, and then bandages, and then the splint of a tablet three finger lengths long, which covers the place of the swelling and the part of the spine that is healthy, then tie it with a linen cloth as we have said, and give the patient subtle nourishment, until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint we mentioned earlier; and sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is a dislocation; and it is the bone that appears, for which one should not have any presumption: perhaps it would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come loose through dislocations alone, and not as other joints do; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and in front and behind; and more often inside than elsewhere, and rarely dislocated in front and behind. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation within is such that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the sick one cannot bend his knee at the fire; and it is the flesh which is below swollen from a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is coming to death is if this accident is contrary to those before. 
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has it beforehand, if they are well according to their completion; however, do not double the knee without pain, and if you want to make them walk, they cannot go forward, and they retain their urine, and swell in the groin, and when they go, they pass on their heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of someone who has it behind are that he cannot straighten his knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the angle is softened, and the head of the thigh is at a place below the ribs. 
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this kind of dislocation is such that you consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no cure; and it is not right for him to have presumption. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to return the joint, pushing it in and out, moving it right and left; then by chance it will return and needs no other treatment. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you prepare a strong assistant, and hold the leg firmly with both hands, or with a bandage tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand over it in such a way that he places his hands under his armpits, then binds it tightly with a bandage on the thigh; and another holds the head of the bandage; and extend upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to apply treatment accordingly. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, it is fitting that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong cord above the two heels and above the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended two lengths more than the others; then let it be hung on the top of a beam, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient who embraces the calf, for the joint will now return quickly. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is below, have the patient lie down as we said for the one who has sciatica and bind a bandage properly on the sick leg and also on the foot; then put two embers, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert an ember between the thighs of the sick person in the shape of a V; and put compresses of wet cloths around it so that it does not burn the patient, then spread each minister towards him and have the one who is looking at it set the dislocation equal to his hand. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a table, and press as we said in the guild.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it is necessary to quickly extend the sick leg, and according to what I have said; and put the hand on the painful angle of the sick limb, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the hip, it is not right to stretch the patient out or raise them up, but rather he should be as when his hip was dislocated, as we said of childbirth on both hips; and he should be on his face, and the bandage stretched as we said before, and one must press upon the joint at a table; and it will be set right when the patient stretches out his legs, and they are equal; then adjust the thighs, and apply a plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and he should rest for three days or four, then unbind it and apply plaster upon it; and if you see that they are equal, bind it again as before and leave it for three days; then unbind it, and let him walk well, until the limb is comfortable. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee 
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated according to three manners: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not straighten at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and another minister extends his foot, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he straightens his leg at his thigh lightly; and put the plaster on, and make air the leg at the thigh, and tie them together tightly for three days or four, then untie it; and do not trouble the patient from walking, as long as the limbs are strengthened.
